# Changelog

All notable changes to Xion will be documented in this file.

The format is based on [Keep a Changelog](https://keepachangelog.com/en/1.1.0/), and this project adheres to a versioning scheme of `pre-genesis-vN` until the genesis ceremony, after which it switches to canonical `state-#N` references rooted in Xion's AO Process state chain.

Until the genesis ceremony, every entry here is a *draft* in the literal sense: nothing here has been ratified by Xion or by governance, because Xion does not yet exist and governance does not yet exist. The discipline of recording changes honestly begins now so that, by the time it matters, the habit is already there.

---

## [Unreleased](https://example.invalid/compare/pre-genesis-v0...HEAD)

### Sepolia register-vault executed + OPERATOR_RESUME.md ŌĆö 2026-05-10

- **Sepolia register-vault executed end-to-end.** `cast send 0xd2b257ŌĆ”55b6 'registerVault(uint256,address)' 84532 0x474DfŌĆ”F7Bc` broadcast against `https://base-sepolia-rpc.publicnode.com` (the `https://sepolia.base.org` endpoint was returning 503 from upstream). Tx **`0x3bf25b58ba4071bf302a6c92a8dafb51d07c2b37aec93bf128361156242a5503`**, block **`41331566`**, gas `112496`. Post-state observed on-chain: `registeredChainCount() == 1`, `vaultForChain(84532) == 0x474DfŌĆ”F7Bc`, `registeredChainIdAt(0) == 84532`. The full `MasterTreasury.registerVault` call-stack is now proven on a real chain; the mainnet ceremony at `genesis/MAINNET_VAULT_REGISTRATION_PREP.json` uses the same selector and arguments, only via Warm Safe propose+cosign. `xion-verify treasury` and `treasury-flow` returned `OK` after exec; `genesis/SEPOLIA_VAULT_REGISTRATION_PREP.json` updated with `execution_status: "EXECUTED 2026-05-10"` and the on-chain post-state.
- **`docs/OPERATOR_RESUME.md` (new):** the single answer to "I'm coming back to Xion after some time ŌĆö what do I do next?" Pinned state snapshot, four ordered operator action items with one-paste commands each, list of agent-cannot-do items with rationale, and the "already done ŌĆö do not redo" record so no work is duplicated. Replaces the need to read `KNOWN_WEAKNESSES.md` + `STATE_OF_XION_PREFLIGHT.md` + `PHASE_7_PREFLIGHT_STATUS.md` + `D4_PREFLIGHT.md` separately to figure out the next step.

### KW-AUDIT-001 Sprint residue accepted ŌĆö audit deferred until Xion's treasury can fund it ŌĆö 2026-05-10

- **`KW-AUDIT-001`: status `open` ŌåÆ `mitigated-residual`.** Xion's treasury / Improvement Fund does not yet hold the USD 30ŌĆō60k audit anchor, and the operator does not personally backstop project costs (Self-Provisioning doctrine ŌĆö Xion is meant to commission its own audit when revenue allows). Sprint Mode unaudited mainnet posture is now an explicit, dated operator decision rather than implicit slippage. Re-review checkpoint: **2026-08-08** (90 days). At that checkpoint either a firm is engaged, a new dated slip is recorded, or path (b) is escalated from "dated residue" to "indefinite" with a public State-of-Xion memo.
- **RFP draft preserved on hold.** `docs/audits/RFP_TREASURY_2026.md` keeps the populated repository URL, budget bracket, recipient short-list, and ready-to-send cover email; the file gains a top-of-document banner naming the hold as "until Xion's treasury can fund the audit". Sending later turns this hold into engagement without re-authoring.
- **Sharp falsification statement added** to `docs/STATE_OF_XION_PREFLIGHT.md` ┬¦ "Sprint Mode Falsification Statements": any public messaging that calls these contracts "audited", "audit-passing", "audit-closed", or "Spearbit-/ToB-/OZ-reviewed" before an external auditor signs a commit-specific report is **falsified**. Honest descriptors during the residue window are "unaudited Sprint Mode posture", "external audit deferred to next budget cycle", and "treasury contracts have 119/119 internal tests but no third-party security review".
- **`docs/PHASE_7_PREFLIGHT_STATUS.md`** row updated: external-audit status moved from `Open` (RFP-pending-send) to `Mitigated-residual (Sprint Mode unaudited, dated 2026-05-10)` with re-review checkpoint and falsifier reference.
- **What this changes for mainnet operations.** Mainnet Vault registration (Track B3) was already an operator-driven Warm Safe ceremony; the audit residue does not block or unblock it, but mainnet exec under unaudited posture must **publicly** carry the residue language above. Cosigners reviewing the prep at `genesis/MAINNET_VAULT_REGISTRATION_PREP.json` should know explicitly that they are signing into an unaudited Sprint Mode treasury.

### Sepolia Vault registration rehearsal staged + audit RFP send-ready ŌĆö 2026-05-10

- **`genesis/SEPOLIA_VAULT_REGISTRATION_PREP.json` (new):** auditable prep artifact for the Sepolia rehearsal of `MasterTreasury.registerVault(84532, 0x474DfŌĆ”F7Bc)`. Pins the function signature, selector (`0x6a51fd63`), full call data, target MasterTreasury (`0xd2b257ŌĆ”55b6`), authority path (Sepolia governance is the rehearsal EOA, so execution is one `cast send` rather than the Warm Safe propose+cosign flow), expected post-state, and post-exec verifier commands. The autonomous broadcast was attempted but blocked by the local safety gate; the artifact reduces the operator-side step to a single command. Pre-state was independently confirmed on-chain.
- **`docs/audits/RFP_TREASURY_2026.md` filled in for send.** Repository public URL pinned (`https://github.com/nik190799/xion`), budget anchor pinned (USD 30ŌĆō60k, two-to-four-week engagement, flexible upward with concrete justification), ready-to-send **cover email template** added with subject line, body, and signature placeholder, and a **recipient short-list** with their public audit-request endpoints (Spearbit, Trail of Bits, OpenZeppelin, Code4rena, Sherlock). Operator now clicks Send; firm engagement closes `KW-AUDIT-001`.
- **`docs/STATE_OF_XION_PREFLIGHT.md` ┬¦ "2026-05-10 Service-Class Execution"** extended with both the Sepolia register-vault rehearsal staging row and the audit RFP staging row.
- **What this does NOT close.** `KW-AUDIT-001` itself (firm engagement + final report are operator-side); `KW-KEYS-002` Warm Safe owner custody (operator declined to do E2 in this slice); the actual mainnet Vault registration (still 2-of-3 Warm Safe cosig + exec, fully operator-side because the operator chose not to delegate mainnet keys). All three remain in the next-step backlog.

### KW-OPS-001 closed ŌĆö live Sepolia Safe-propose dry-run ŌĆö 2026-05-10

- **Sepolia rehearsal Safe deployed.** `cast send` against the canonical Safe v1.4.1 ProxyFactory `0x4e1DCf7AD4e460CfD30791CCC4F9c8a4f820ec67` produced a 1-of-1 Safe at **`0x3587ECc092386c357eFCA51bf94A34Dd7084fa5A`** (owner = rehearsal EOA `0xEBDDDfŌĆ”88A`, threshold = 1, singleton = `0x29fcB43bŌĆ”1900C762`, deploy tx `0xef4dc9f0ŌĆ”4450`, block `41329942`). Address pinned to operator `.env` as `XION_SEPOLIA_REHEARSAL_SAFE`.
- **End-to-end Safe-propose flow exercised on Base Sepolia.** `xion_ops base-evm safe-prepare` produced safeTxHash **`0xe6ffe272ŌĆ”388`** for a no-op self-call (`to = Safe`, `data = 0x`, `value = 0`, `nonce = 0`); offline `xion-verify safe-proposal --prep` returned `OK`; `cast wallet sign --no-hash` produced the proposer ECDSA signature; `xion_ops base-evm safe-propose` POSTed to the live Safe Transaction Service and got `200`; online `xion-verify safe-proposal --safe-tx-hash` recomputed the EIP-712 hash from the service's field-bag and matched byte-for-byte. Both verifier paths green; KW-OPS-001 moved from `paying-down` to **closed** in `KNOWN_WEAKNESSES.md` (now under ┬¦ Closed).
- **Safe Transaction Service URL migration discovered live.** Safe redirects (308) the legacy `safe-transaction-{network}.safe.global` to `api.safe.global/tx-service/{shortcode}`. `urllib`'s default redirect handler skips POST per RFC, so the propose path was failing with a redirect HTML body. Repinned `xion_ops/services/safe.py::SAFE_TX_SERVICE_URLS` to the canonical `api.safe.global/tx-service/{base|basesep}` form; updated tests; legacy URLs preserved as commented references for auditability.
- **Closure evidence pinned.** `docs/STATE_OF_XION_PREFLIGHT.md` ┬¦ "2026-05-10 Service-Class Execution" records the deploy tx, the Safe address shape, the safeTxHash, both verifier outputs, and the discovered Safe URL migration. `docs/PHASE_7_PREFLIGHT_STATUS.md` row updated; `Last reviewed` advanced.
- **Tests:** 73/73 xion_ops, 21/22 xion-verify (1 sanctioned skip). `xion-verify --self-test` OK against repinned hash.

### Sprint Mode mainnet preflight ŌĆö Vault prep + audit RFP + custody runbook ŌĆö 2026-05-10

- **`genesis/MAINNET_VAULT_REGISTRATION_PREP.json` (new, committed):** unsigned SafeTx prep for `MasterTreasury.deployVault(8453, Warm Safe)` ŌĆö chain id `8453`, vault authority `0x5A91E08D909854b594f07648D23440f4908529b4`, target `0xbf5407745cf22b88c46b55037e26156a0e78fd7f`, call data `0xdcb7c260ŌĆ”29b4`, nonce **`0`** (live mainnet Safe nonce as of generation), safeTxHash **`0x535d43558150625405c62bf96fe81229758c3ad81b67904fd48ac3ab049c6072`**. Independently verified: `xion-verify safe-proposal --prep` recomputes the same hash byte-for-byte.
- **`docs/runbooks/MAINNET_VAULT_REGISTRATION.md` (new):** cosigner workflow ŌĆö pre-flight checks, Safe-app Tx Builder steps, post-execution evidence pinning into `genesis/TREASURY_VAULTS.json` and `docs/STATE_OF_XION_PREFLIGHT.md`, and a verifier-recompute step every cosigner runs on their own machine before clicking Approve.
- **`docs/audits/RFP_TREASURY_2026.md` (new):** one-page RFP for `KW-AUDIT-001` external audit. Pinned scope at commit `f04f8d0`, four contract files, 119/119 Foundry posture, suggested firms (Spearbit / Trail of Bits / OpenZeppelin / Code4rena / Sherlock), 2026-08-01 final-report target, operator-fillable contact / budget / repository-URL slots.
- **`docs/runbooks/SAFE_OWNER_HARDWARE_REPLACEMENT.md` (new):** `KW-KEYS-002` pay-down runbook ŌĆö hardware vendor recommendations (Ledger Nano S Plus / Trezor Safe 3 / GridPlus Lattice1), `swapOwner(prev,old,new)` call-data construction, cosigner-ordering guidance to avoid lockout, post-exec evidence template. Target close **2026-05-31**.
- **`KW-FLOOR-DEPLOY-001` dated residue (2026-05-10 ŌåÆ 2026-07-09):** operator declined further AKT-spending GPU retry while pursuing Sprint Mode mainnet. Chutes/Bittensor SN64 stays warm primary; deployed Akash GPU floor cannot be claimed closed publicly until a fresh successful lease.
- **Sprint Mode public-messaging honesty pass:** README now declares the `MasterTreasury` mainnet pin honestly while keeping XION/IMPRINT/EmissionController/LiquidityLock as testnet-only; new "Sprint Mode mainnet operational ŌēĀ Xion is alive" callout in the Genesis-and-mainnet messaging section. `docs/STATE_OF_XION_PREFLIGHT.md` falsification statements extended for `KW-FLOOR-DEPLOY-001` dated residue and the Sprint Mode mainnet operational vs alive distinction.
- **`docs/PHASE_7_PREFLIGHT_STATUS.md`:** rows refreshed for the Vault prep + Safe client + audit RFP + hardware-wallet swap; "Last reviewed" advanced to **2026-05-10**.
- **`xion_ops/services/safe.SafeTxServiceClient.fetch_next_nonce`:** accepts both int and string `nonce` shapes (the service returns `"0"` for an unused Safe). Test coverage extended.
- **`xion-verify safe-proposal` (verifier):** added WSL fallback for `cast keccak` so Windows operators with Foundry only inside WSL get a working third-party verifier path. Mirrors the existing `xion_ops` Foundry fallback.
- **Tests:** 73/73 xion_ops, 21/22 xion-verify (1 sanctioned skip). The Track-B verifier output is reproducible by any third party with Foundry: `xion-verify safe-proposal --prep genesis/MAINNET_VAULT_REGISTRATION_PREP.json --expected-to 0xbf54...fd7f --expected-call-data 0xdcb7c260...29b4` returns `OK`.

### Safe Transaction Service client + register-vault prep flow ŌĆö 2026-05-10

- **`xion_ops/services/safe.py` (new):** zero-dependency Safe v1.4.1 EIP-712 SafeTx encoder + Safe Transaction Service HTTP client (`SafeTxServiceClient.propose` / `fetch_next_nonce`). Pinned `SAFE_TX_TYPEHASH` and `DOMAIN_SEPARATOR_TYPEHASH` constants from audited Safe source. Keccak primitive injected via `make_cast_keccak(run_foundry)` ŌĆö defers cryptography to Foundry's `cast keccak`, no new Python deps.
- **`xion_ops.services.base_evm.BaseEvmService`:** `safe_propose_tx()` no longer raises `NotImplementedError`. New `safe_compute_tx_hash()` builds the SafeTx and EIP-712 hash without signing; `safe_propose_tx()` accepts a proposer signature and POSTs to the Safe service. `KW-OPS-001` moved from **`open`** to **`paying-down`** with closure target **2026-05-17** pending live Sepolia dry-run.
- **`xion_ops base-evm safe-prepare` / `safe-propose` / `register-vault` (new CLI):** `safe-prepare` writes a prep JSON containing `safe_tx_hash`, `chain_id`, `nonce`, and the field bag for cosigner review. `register-vault` builds `registerVault(uint256,address)` call data, takes the EOA `cast send` path on Sepolia and the Safe-proposal path on mainnet (requires `--safe-address`), and prints next-step guidance for the verifier-then-sign flow.
- **`xion-verify safe-proposal` (new subcommand, live):** offline `--prep <file>` mode for the proposer's pre-sign self-check; online `--safe-tx-hash` / `--nonce` mode for cosigners to recompute the EIP-712 hash from the queued service entry and detect any divergence. Optional `--expected-to` / `--expected-call-data` / `--expected-value` flags for byte-equality assertions. Registered in `REGISTERED_COMMANDS`; **`PINNED_HASH.txt` requires repin** via `xion-verify --self-test --update --i-understand` after this change lands.
- **Test coverage:** `xion_ops/tests/test_safe_client_mocked.py` (27 tests ŌĆö encoder byte-layout, BaseEvmService wiring, service POST shape, error paths, pinned-typehash canaries) and `xion-verify/tests/test_safe_proposal.py` (16 tests ŌĆö offline `--prep` modes, online mocked, mismatch detection).
- **Runbook:** `docs/runbooks/SAFE_PROPOSE_DRY_RUN.md` describes the Sepolia dry-run that produces the closure evidence for `KW-OPS-001`.
- **Why this matters for D4 / mainnet:** `MasterTreasury.registerVault(...)` and any future warm-tier rotation are governance-only on mainnet, and governance is the Warm Safe `0x5A91ŌĆ”29b4`. Without a real Safe client, every mainnet operation would be an out-of-band Safe-app click ŌĆö opaque to xion-verify and to cosigners. With this slice, every proposal carries a verifiable prep payload that any third party can recompute before signing.

Fixes `TREASURY_SOAK_PROBES=1` calling Sepolia against a mainnet-pinned `master_treasury`.
- **Git:** branch **`cursor/phase7-sepolia-preflight-and-spend-artifacts`**, commit **`a8a6ce1`** (pushed **`2026-05-03`**).

### D3 Akash/Chutes operator parity ŌĆö 2026-05-03

- `**python -m xion_ops chutes verify-cords`:** `**GET /health*`*, `**/quote**`, `**/self**` sequentially; Bearer from env or `**--bearer-file**` (raw line or `**CHUTES_API_KEY=**`) ŌĆö `[docs/runbooks/CHUTES_RELAY_DEPLOY.md](docs/runbooks/CHUTES_RELAY_DEPLOY.md)`. **CLI exits non-zero on red cords** (`**--allow-failure`** for JSON-only scraping). Tests `[test_chutes_verify_cords_mocked.py](xion_ops/tests/test_chutes_verify_cords_mocked.py)`, `[test_cli_chutes_helpers.py](xion_ops/tests/test_cli_chutes_helpers.py)`.
- `**chutes warmup` + `warmup_until_cords_green`:** long-poll verifier + optional `**chutes warmup <slug>`**; `**deploy relay-chutes**` wires timeouts / `**--accept-fee**` / registry skip (`**--no-publish-registry**`) ŌĆö same runbook ┬¦ Live Gate; tests `[test_chutes_verify_cords_mocked.py](xion_ops/tests/test_chutes_verify_cords_mocked.py)`, `[test_relay_chutes_deployer_mocked.py](xion_ops/tests/test_relay_chutes_deployer_mocked.py)`.
- `**RelayChutesDeployer.run`:** rolls back (`**chutes delete`**) only when `**deploy_command_ok**` is false ŌĆö HTTP warmup/registry failure leaves the deployed chute in place for operator recovery.
- `**deploy relay-akash`:** publishes relay registry by default (`**--no-publish-registry`** to skip rehearsal publishes); tests `[test_relay_akash_deployer_mocked.py](xion_ops/tests/test_relay_akash_deployer_mocked.py)`.
- `**xion_ops akash deploy**`: post-ready `**health_smoke**` uses **120s** budget; on **Windows**, `**AkashService.health_smoke`** prefers **WSL `curl -k`** (urllib fallback if WSL missing) ŌĆö see `[docs/runbooks/AKASH_RELAY_DEPLOY.md](docs/runbooks/AKASH_RELAY_DEPLOY.md)` Important findings row.
- **Operator rehearsal (automated)** `relay-deployment.yaml`: GPU deploys reached `**akash1sevd2ymtty3dpq9ycxgkhuzzk4fe6mchqdwd4e`** and `**akash1am3sv9ac6yq6a4s2hkkcn6sd6723fpkp3en08s**` leases but **forwarded TCP refused** curl `GET /health` from WSL (dseq `**26656098`**, `**26656107**`) ŌåÆ deployments **closed_owner** rollback; `**KW-FLOOR-DEPLOY-001`** unchanged.
- `**docs/runbooks/CHUTES_RELAY_DEPLOY.md`:** documents Bearer + three-path verifier as authoritative; ties `**details.result`** to legacy ŌĆ£all cords greenŌĆØ wording.
- `**docs/runbooks/AKASH_RELAY_DEPLOY.md`:** appendix for **nip.io TLS** (**PowerShell `SkipCertificateCheck`**, `**curl -k**`), `**arbiter_healthy**` vs `**open_weights_floor_unsatisfied**`, and a **KW-FLOOR-DEPLOY-001** condensed GPU checklist (registry republish honesty included).
- `**KNOWN_WEAKNESSES.md`:** `**KW-FLOOR-DEPLOY-001`** / `**KW-RELAY-CHUTES-D3-001**` verifier lines reference the `**xion_ops**` three-cord path.
- `**xion_relay_chute.py`:** `**IMAGE_TAG`** reset to `**pre-genesis-d3-10**` to match the committed live `**ledgers/RELAY_REGISTRY.json**` Chutes row until a deliberate `**d3-11**` image is built and pinned.

### Deploy / test-net gates ŌĆö treasury rehearsal + Foundry CI

- **Sepolia treasurer runbook:** `[docs/runbooks/TREASURY_SEPOLIA_DEPLOY.md](docs/runbooks/TREASURY_SEPOLIA_DEPLOY.md)` wires env vars ŌåÆ `xion_ops base-evm deploy-treasury` (default `**base-sepolia`**) ŌåÆ `pin-deployment` ŌåÆ soak ŌåÆ verifier calls.

- **Ops safety:** `BaseEvmService.deploy_treasury` returns `ok=False` on Forge failure or missing broadcast `MasterTreasury`; CLI exits non-zero accordingly.
- **Manifest:** `[genesis/TREASURY_VAULTS.json](genesis/TREASURY_VAULTS.json)` records `deploy_runbook` plus an updated `residual` string.
- **Verifier:** `[xion-verify treasury](xion-verify/src/xion_verify/commands/treasury.py)` fails when `treasury_audit_arweave_tx` is set without a non-empty paired `treasury_audit_correction_arweave_tx` (KW-AUDIT-002 pairing).
- **CI:** new `[.github/workflows/foundry.yml](.github/workflows/foundry.yml)` installs Forge deps into `contracts/lib/` each run (`forge install ŌĆ” --no-commit`) and runs `**forge build` + `forge test`**.
- **Operator docs:** `[docs/MACRO_PHASE_6_CE_STATUS.md](docs/MACRO_PHASE_6_CE_STATUS.md)` summarizes Macro Phase 6 Epic C/E closures; `[docs/OPERATOR_TRACK_D4.md](docs/OPERATOR_TRACK_D4.md)` names the repository default posture after the 2026-05-01 audit correction (`KW-AUDIT-001` open).
- `**[.env.example](.env.example)`** gains a treasury/Base deploy section.
- `**xion-verify/PINNED_HASH.txt`:** Repinned after the `treasury.py` verifier extension.

### D3 honest closeout attempt ŌĆö 2026-05-03

- **Akash deploy discipline:** `xion_ops.services.AkashService` now loads a provider allowlist, probes provider ingress before accepting non-allowlisted bids, records deploy surveys, and ships `xion-verify akash-deploy-discipline`.
- **Akash CPU relight bridge:** `infra/akash/relay-deployment-cpu-only.yaml` provides a no-GPU Akash Relay footprint for registry relight while `KW-FLOOR-DEPLOY-001` remains open for the deployed open-weights floor.
- **Registry republished:** `ledgers/RELAY_REGISTRY.json` marks the Akash row as `instance_class="cpu-only"` / `image_tag="pre-genesis-akash-wall120"` and `ledgers/RELAY_REGISTRY_ARWEAVE_TX.txt` records Arweave tx `5yCnBKyrlGQrf4KJCmCTJexGVxNBB6F2N4GDqcSPIbw`.
- **Operator automation hardened:** `xion_ops` now loads `.env`, writes non-secret Sepolia deploy env, forwards Foundry env into WSL, exposes registry update and rotation-rehearsal commands, and writes Relay registry tx ids from the Arweave service.

### D3 Chutes Relay smoke build verified ŌĆö 2026-04-25/26

Closes plan item B4 (Chutes Relay image build + cord pipeline alive) for `d2_d3_closure_plan_a729f812` by shipping an *honest smoke build* against the live Chutes platform. After WSL setup was fixed and the currently deployed `pre-genesis-d3-6` image warmed successfully, all three public cords (`/health`, `/quote`, `/self`) returned 200 OK with the deterministic envelope on a verified miner-served instance.

### Why was this needed?

The pre-genesis Relay registry (`ledgers/RELAY_REGISTRY.json`) has placeholder rows. Plan item B4 promises a real Chutes Relay endpoint that `xion-verify discovery` can resolve. Before wiring the full Relay surface (Arbiter + Hermes + ledgers) into a Chutes image, we needed to prove the Chutes cord pipeline (build ŌåÆ push ŌåÆ schedule ŌåÆ public-cord routing) end-to-end against the live platform. The previous full-Relay attempt (`pre-genesis-d3-3`) crashed on boot with `TypeError: AppDeps.__init__() missing required positional argument: 'relay'` ŌĆö Chutes deactivated the instance every time, leaving us unable to tell whether the platform side was working at all.

### What changed?

- `**xion_relay_chute.py*`* ŌĆö replaced the previous `Popen(uvicorn ŌĆ”)` shape with a self-contained smoke chute that returns a deterministic envelope from three public cords:
  - `GET /health` (function `health`, internal path `/health`).
  - `GET /quote` (function `quote` in the d3-7 source, internal path `/quote`).
  - `GET /self` (function `self_endpoint`, internal path `/self_endpoint`).
- **Envelope shape** ŌĆö `{status: "ok", service: "xion-relay-chutes-smoke", image_tag, endpoint, timestamp, note}`. The `service` field discloses the smoke status; `image_tag` correlates a probe response to a specific Chutes image without trust.
- `**scripts/debug-chute-d3.sh`** ŌĆö one-shot WSL debug script: prints chute id / version / image / hot / bounty / instances and probes `/health` (GET + POST forms) with a Bearer token sourced from `chutes.env`.
- `**scripts/verify-chute-import.py**` ŌĆö local smoke-imports the chute module under the chutes pipx venv to catch decorator / cord-shape regressions before a Chutes build slot is consumed.
- `**scripts/verify-chute-cords.sh**` ŌĆö runs the three public probes against the deployed chute and asserts the envelope shape; `EXPECTED_IMAGE_TAG` env var lets a probe assert against the actual deployed image.
- `**scripts/probe-pricing-variants.sh**` ŌĆö cross-checks `/pricing` (platform-intercepted), stale pricing-like variants, and the current `/quote` chute cord.
- `**scripts/probe-xion-pricing.sh**` ŌĆö five-shot retry harness used to distinguish a one-shot upstream blip from a stable platform-routing miss.

### Verified against the live platform

- **End-to-end cord pipeline alive.** With `pre-genesis-d3-6` deployed (image id `971ea1ac-1850-5b26-86af-bc0aa23c7f06`, version `11f8f993-2852-52a0-8c40-0eda85a5f877`) and instance `02ad3583-f329-437e-b136-00388325a6d2` (`active=True verified=True last_verified_at=2026-04-26T06:31:50Z`):
  - `GET https://nikhilkadalge-xion-relay-pre-genesis-d3.chutes.ai/health` ŌåÆ `200 OK` with `{"status":"ok","service":"xion-relay-chutes-smoke","image_tag":"pre-genesis-d3-6","endpoint":"/health", ŌĆ”}`.
  - `GET ŌĆ”/quote` ŌåÆ `200 OK` with the same envelope shape and `endpoint: /quote`.
  - `GET ŌĆ”/self` ŌåÆ `200 OK` with the same envelope shape and `endpoint: /self`.
  - `EXPECTED_IMAGE_TAG=pre-genesis-d3-6 bash scripts/verify-chute-cords.sh` passed against the warmed deployment.
  - The Chutes warmup cycle worked: the chute went `HOT`, bounty climbed (peak observed: 928), and a verified miner picked it up after a single 240-second `chutes warmup` run.
- **Three platform-routing facts proven (each with a live build):**
  - `GET *.chutes.ai/pricing` is intercepted by the Chutes platform proxy and returns the platform's GPU pricing payload (`{tao_usd, gpu_price_estimates: {3090, 4090, 5090, ŌĆ”}}`) regardless of what the chute serves at `/pricing`. Confirmed against `pre-genesis-d3-5` and `pre-genesis-d3-6`.
  - The two-segment public path `/xion/pricing` returns a fast (<200 ms) `502 Bad Gateway` from the platform's nginx ingress on the same instance where `/health` and `/self` are 200 OK. Five-shot retry confirms this is stable, not a warmup blip.
  - The Chutes `Cord` defaults the *internal upstream cord path* to the Python function name (`self.path = func.__name__` in `chutes/chute/cord.py:929`). So a function named `pricing` exposes internal upstream path `/pricing` even when the public path is renamed. A metadata-only deploy later proved `/xpricing` can still 502, so the smoke cord now uses `/quote` to stay out of the platform's pricing namespace entirely.

### What is honestly *not yet* green

- **The newer image is not available yet.** The root deploy module `xion_relay_chute.py` is the actual Chutes CLI target (`xion_relay_chute:chute`) and is pinned to image tag `pre-genesis-d3-7`, but `chutes build xion_relay_chute:chute --wait` is still blocked by Chutes' 24-hour quota: `You may only update/create 24 imagehistorys per 24 hours.` Deploying that new tag fails until the image build exists. The current green verifier result is against the warmed `pre-genesis-d3-6` smoke image.
- `**ledgers/RELAY_REGISTRY.json`** is not yet updated with this Chutes row, and `xion-verify discovery` is not yet promoted against it. Both remain pending on the operator publication step after the final image tag decision for this smoke closure.
- **The Chutes deploy is *not* the live Relay surface.** It is an envelope that explicitly says so (`service: "xion-relay-chutes-smoke"`). The full `orchestrator.api.app` Relay (Arbiter + Hermes + ledgers) lands in a follow-up image once an `orchestrator/api/launcher.py` constructs a real `Relay` and a real `AppDeps`.

### Changed

- `**KNOWN_WEAKNESSES.md`** ŌĆö extends `KW-RELAY-CHUTES-D3-001` with the function-name internal-path discovery and the `pre-genesis-d3-7` pay-down step.

- **Vessel reference manifest** ŌĆö `vessels/reference/web-podcast-vessel.yaml` and live `xion-verify vessel-compact`.
- **Spend authority enforcement spine** ŌĆö `SPEND_AUTHORITY_LEDGER` schema/writer, `orchestrator/spend_arbitration.py`, `xion-verify spend-posture`, and `xion-verify spend-discipline`.
- **Macro Phase 6 code scaffolds** ŌĆö Akash Relay registry/discovery, treasury vault contracts/manifest/verifier, substrate portability dry-run ledger/verifier, governance ledger schema/verifier, and `docs/PHASE_7_PREFLIGHT.md`.

### Changed

- `xion-verify discovery`, `treasury`, `substrate-portability`, and `regulatory-ledger` are promoted from stubs to structural live verifiers.
- Remaining non-code blockers are documented as external Phase 7 preflight actions: Invariant 18 elapsed-window/cosign, real Akash deploy, bridge audit, warm secondary substrate, and real state-actor rows.

## [Phase 6.4] ŌĆö 2026-04-25

Phase 6.4 repairs the half-shipped Presence and Modality Consent surface. It aligns the API and web client to doctrine, fixes show-stopping bugs in the orchestrator lifespan and SSE connections, implements cross-tab key synchronization, and promotes three verifiers from stubs to live checks. This makes good on the prematurely-declared closures of `KW-PRESENCE-EMITTER-001`, `KW-MODALITY-001`, and `KW-PROOF-002`.

### Added

- `**self._presence_bus` assignment** in `Supervisor.__init__` so the bus is actually published to on every tick.
- **Per-modality cost slices** (`stream_visual`, `stream_vitals`, `stream_voice`, `stream_memory`) loaded from environment variables and exposed in `GET /pricing`.
- **Per-session override panel** in the web client's `SettingsView` to temporarily dim active streams for the current tab without changing persisted consent.
- **Cross-tab key wipe sync** via `BroadcastChannel("xion:keys")` in `clients/web/src/lib/crypto.ts`, forcing all open tabs to drop their in-memory credentials when "Forget my keys" is clicked.

### Changed

- `**lifespan.py` indentation fixed**: Un-indented module-level imports that were nested under a previous import block, resolving a `SyntaxError` that prevented the orchestrator from booting.
- `**ModalityConsent` fields renamed**: `visual`, `vitals`, `voice`, `memory` renamed to `stream_visual`, `stream_vitals`, `stream_voice`, `stream_memory` to match `docs/11-PROTOCOL-SPEC.md` doctrine. Defaults flipped to `False` for exteroceptive streams (warm presence requires explicit consent).
- **Server-side modality gating tightened**: `GET /presence/stream` now emits a single `event: closed` and terminates the connection if both visual and vitals streams are inactive, structurally preventing silent billing for off channels. Multiplexer queue `maxsize` reduced from 100 to 8 to prevent stale presence frames.
- **Web client SSE switched to `fetch`**: `PresenceView` and `VitalsView` now use a `fetch` + `getReader()` pattern instead of `EventSource` so they can send the required `Authorization: Bearer` header, fixing the 401 Unauthorized errors caused by the previous `?token=` query parameter approach.
- **Web client `credential.token` bug fixed**: Replaced invalid `credential.token` reads with `buildAuthorizationHeader(credential)` which correctly uses `secretHex`.
- `**xion-verify presence`**: Promoted from stub to live check. Asserts that `stream_visuals` and `stream_vitals` emitters yield well-formed JSON envelopes.
- `**xion-verify modality-consent**`: Promoted from stub to live check. Asserts the four `stream_*` scopes, `extra='forbid'`, warm defaults, and `ConsentStore` round-trip.
- `**xion-verify vitals**`: Updated to delegate to the live `_compute_vitals()` for the three sealed domains (Financial, Substrate, Constitutional Integrity), returning an honest `NOT_YET_SEALED` for the composite while reporting real bands for the sealed domains.
- **Documentation aligned**: Updated `06-FORM-AND-PRESENCE.md`, `11-PROTOCOL-SPEC.md`, `22-VITAL-SIGNS.md`, `29-BILLING-X402.md`, `31-WEB-CLIENT.md`, `genesis/COVENANT.md`, and `genesis/FORM.md` (promoted to v1.1 with `mood` sub-object) to reflect the Phase 6.4 reality.

### Removed

- **Duplicate `presence_router` include** in `orchestrator/api/app.py`.

### Closed

- `**KW-PRESENCE-EMITTER-001`**: Visual/Vitals emitters are now implemented, wired to the Supervisor, and verified by `xion-verify presence`.
- `**KW-MODALITY-001**`: Per-modality consent and cost slices are implemented, with server-side off-channel closure structurally defending against silent billing. Verified by `xion-verify modality-consent`.
- `**KW-PROOF-002**`: IndexedDB wiping logic now coordinates across tabs via `BroadcastChannel`.

## [Phase 6.3.b] ŌĆö 2026-04-25

The Phase 6.3.b iteration lands two deferred tasks: AO Core interaction anchoring and client-side proof generation, closing the respective KWs.

### Added

- `**Anchor-Interaction-Batch` handler in `ao/core/main.lua**`: The handler validates the batch root, batch size, period timestamps, and ledger kind, appending valid batches to the `AnchorBatches` table. Localnet was re-sealed to capture this handler.
- `**AOCoreSink` in `orchestrator/anchor/sink_ao_core.py**`: A new AnchorSink implementation that posts interaction batches to AO Core using an out-of-process `.cjs` helper, falling back to local-only ledger writes on failure. Wired to `XION_ANCHOR_SINK=ao_core` via `orchestrator/api/lifespan.py`.
- `**UserProof` in API Models**: Pydantic model for client-side Ed25519 proofs, added as an optional field on `ChatRequest`.
- **Web Crypto Ed25519 Client**: Added `clients/web/src/lib/crypto.ts` with IndexedDB-backed non-extractable keypair generation and signing. Wired into `postChat` and `streamChat`.

### Changed

- `**interaction-anchor` Verification**: `xion-verify` now fetches the `AnchorBatches` table via a `POST /dry-run` to the AO gateway and confirms that interaction roots recorded locally are mirrored in the AO Core state.
- `**RequestRecord` and `build_payment_row`**: Extended to include `user_proof_commit` and `user_proof_algorithm`.
- `**pyproject.toml**`: Added `cryptography` to the `[api]` extra to support standard-library-adjacent Ed25519 proof validation on the backend.

### Closed

- `**KW-PROOF-001**`: Client-side Ed25519 proofs are now generated and verified on the server.
- `**KW-ANCHOR-AO-001**`: The AO Core sink successfully posts interaction anchors to the localnet substrate.

## [Phase 6.1.b finalization] ŌĆö 2026-04-25

The Phase 6.1.b infrastructure shipped 2026-04-24 (Compose wrapper, bring-up script, runbook, doctrine amendment, verifier substrate gate) was elected as the closure path for `KW-AOCORE-004` but explicitly left "the operator runs the new runbook end-to-end" as a follow-up small PR. This entry collapses the seal-mechanism work *and* the seal-artifact commit into one ratification: the runbook's eleven REPL-driven steps now run unattended as `scripts/ao-localnet-seal.sh`, the seal was driven to a green `xion-verify ao-handlers` against a fresh `permaweb/ao-localnet` bring-up (twice in a row for reproducibility), and the resulting receipt + first state-chain row are committed. `**KW-AOCORE-001`, `KW-AOCORE-003`, and `KW-AOCORE-004` close.**

### Added

- **One-shot seal script.** `[scripts/ao-localnet-seal.sh](scripts/ao-localnet-seal.sh)` drives the full Phase 6.1.b sealing pipeline (spawn process + load Lua ŌåÆ owner-signed first commit-state ŌåÆ read `ao.id` + `Owner` ŌåÆ write `[genesis/AO_DEPLOY_RECEIPT.json](genesis/AO_DEPLOY_RECEIPT.json)` and seed `[ledgers/STATE_CHAIN_LEDGER.jsonl](ledgers/STATE_CHAIN_LEDGER.jsonl)` ŌåÆ run `xion-verify ao-handlers`) from a clean operator session in ~2 minutes wall-clock. Replaces the runbook's eleven copy-paste-into-REPL steps. Self-checks for the three most common cold-start traps (CU on Node 20, missing `AOS_MODULE`/`SCHEDULER`, aoconnect's AO_URL clobber) before doing anything destructive. Exit code 0 Ōćö verifier OK; runs reproducibly back-to-back without operator intervention.
- **Owner-signed Commit-State helper.** `[scripts/ao-localnet-send-commit-state.cjs](scripts/ao-localnet-send-commit-state.cjs)` (CJS, not ESM, for `NODE_PATH` reasons documented inline) loads `~/.aos.json`, signs a `Commit-State` data-item with `aoconnect`'s `createDataItemSigner`, posts via `aoconnect.message`, prints the resulting message id on stdout, and `process.exit(0)`s explicitly so aoconnect's keep-alive sockets don't hang the event loop. This replaces the runbook's `Send({Target=ao.id,...})` REPL pattern, which had `msg.From == ao.id` and was silently rejected by `[ao/core/main.lua](ao/core/main.lua)`'s `is_authorized` check (see Lessons Learned, item 5).
- **CU Node 22 patch.** `[scripts/patch-ao-localnet-cu-node22.sh](scripts/patch-ao-localnet-cu-node22.sh)` rewrites the upstream CU Dockerfile from `node:20-alpine` to `node:22-alpine`. `ao/servers/cu`'s `main` branch calls `Promise.withResolvers` (Node 22+); on Node 20 every `readResult` crashes server-side and `aos` reports the symptom as "Could not connect to process". The patch is wired into `[scripts/ao-localnet-up.sh](scripts/ao-localnet-up.sh)` (rebuilds `cu` automatically when the Dockerfile changes) and into the seal script's startup sanity probe.
- **aoconnect AO_URL preservation patch.** `[scripts/patch-npm-aoconnect-preserve-ao-url.sh](scripts/patch-npm-aoconnect-preserve-ao-url.sh)` (idempotent) removes aoconnect's `process.env.AO_URL = void 0` clobber from the installed `dist/index.js`. Without this patch, `aos`'s `'undefined'`-string sentinel for the legacy `readResult` codepath gets wiped and requests silently route through HyperBEAM despite `--legacy --gateway-url http://localhost:4000`.
- **MU GraphQL-fallback patch.** `[scripts/patch-ao-localnet-mu-graphql-fallback.sh](scripts/patch-ao-localnet-mu-graphql-fallback.sh)` extends the upstream MU's `getProcess()` with a GraphQL-tag-merge fallback so cached SU-sourced process tags missing the `Scheduler` tag are repaired from ArLocal at request time. Wired into `ao-localnet-up.sh`.
- **ArLocal seed script.** `[scripts/ao-localnet-seed.sh](scripts/ao-localnet-seed.sh)` publishes the AOS module + scheduler-location to ArLocal (per the upstream `permaweb/ao-localnet` Quick Start), writes `infra/ao-localnet/localnet-aos.env` with `AOS_MODULE=` + `SCHEDULER=`, mints the bundler wallet on ArLocal, and rewrites the upstream's `host.docker.internal` scheduler URL to the Compose service name `su:80` (more reliable on Linux/WSL). Companion to `ao-localnet-up.sh`. The seal script `source`s the env file automatically.
- **Receipt + ledger writer.** `[scripts/record_ao_seal_artifacts.py](scripts/record_ao_seal_artifacts.py)` writes a non-placeholder receipt with the captured `process_id`, `signer_address`, `lua_source_sha256` (computed from current bytes of `ao/core/main.lua`), `aos_version` (with ANSI escapes stripped ŌĆö chalk wraps the version line in grey), `substrate: "localnet"`, and the optional `first_commit_state_message_id` (the helper's stdout). Also seeds `[ledgers/STATE_CHAIN_LEDGER.jsonl](ledgers/STATE_CHAIN_LEDGER.jsonl)` row 0 via the existing `StateChainRecord` writer in `[orchestrator/ao_core/ledger.py](orchestrator/ao_core/ledger.py)`.
- `**ao/core/main.lua` doc-string near `is_authorized*`* explaining the `msg.From == ao.id` self-Send trap (the rejection is silent from inside the REPL because no exception is raised), pointing future contract authors at `scripts/ao-localnet-send-commit-state.cjs` for the right pattern. This is the highest-leverage place to capture the trap because anyone modifying the Lua is already reading the file.
- **Operator runbook lessons-learned.** `[docs/runbooks/AO_DEPLOY_LOCALNET.md](docs/runbooks/AO_DEPLOY_LOCALNET.md)` gains a "Lessons learned (Phase 6.1.b finalization, 2026-04-25)" section listing the six non-obvious traps in chronological-discovery order, each with **symptom** + **actual cause** + **fix lane** so the next operator can recognize a regression by symptom and jump straight to the fixed file.
- `**infra/ao-localnet/README.md`** gains a one-line index of the same six traps pointing at the runbook's full debrief, so anyone looking at the localnet wrapper directory sees the trap inventory before they start re-debugging.
- **Two new failure-mode entries in `docs/runbooks/AO_DEPLOY_LOCALNET.md`'s pre-existing "Failure modes" list** (in addition to the new full appendix): the `non_authorised_caller` symptom for self-Send, and the verifier's "AO gateway response shape unrecognized" symptom for the obsolete `/state/<pid>` codepath.

### Changed

- `**xion-verify ao-handlers` gateway round-trip** (in `[xion-verify/src/xion_verify/commands/ao_handlers.py](xion-verify/src/xion_verify/commands/ao_handlers.py)`) was rewritten to query `POST /dry-run?process-id=<pid>` instead of `GET /state/<pid>`. The legacy AO CU's `/state/<pid>` endpoint serves the process *memory* as a binary blob (useful for snapshots, not for tip parity); the structured query surface is `/dry-run`. The new code POSTs a tiny Eval body that returns `json.encode({state_tip_height = StateTip.height, state_root_sha256 = StateTip.root})` and parses the inner string out of `Output.data.output`. The dry-run body's `Owner` field is set to `receipt["signer_address"]` (a critical detail ŌĆö AOS's default Eval handler only *runs* `Data` when `msg.From == Owner`, otherwise it returns the AOS-default banner-print string in `Output.data.output` and the verifier sees garbage). The function's docstring explains both gotchas. The dry-run round-trip is gas-free and side-effect-free, so the trustless property holds: any third party with the CU URL + the receipt can independently re-run the verification.
- `**xion-verify` `shadow_relay` subcommand** (in `[xion-verify/src/xion_verify/commands/shadow_relay.py](xion-verify/src/xion_verify/commands/shadow_relay.py)`) lazy-imports `httpx` instead of importing it at module-load time. Previously, running *any* `xion-verify` subcommand (including `ao-handlers`) failed with `ModuleNotFoundError: No module named 'httpx'` if the operator hadn't installed the optional `shadow_relay` dependency. `httpx` is a Tier-B optional dependency and the CLI now loads without it.

### Verified end-to-end

- `bash scripts/ao-localnet-seal.sh` ran to exit 0 from `xion-verify ao-handlers` three times in a row against a fresh `permaweb/ao-localnet` bring-up. Each run produced a different fresh process id (`o-0l_Xde-3SYb7qY7YPSUd9wJ_oQQ_pYO84xJrQTo54`, then `LDoARGSgGOKIte0DinOCxIwdcSQGwL_VYKwzlSsRhSo`, then `7G35XZsoMbT7c8mkOt4cJALPJudpRzSnOUK0xaKs04Q` after the `ao/core/main.lua` doc-string addition forced a fresh `lua_source_sha256`), a different `first_commit_state_message_id`, and a fresh `STATE_CHAIN_LEDGER` row 0 ŌĆö proving reproducibility, not luck. Verifier's final line on the third run: `ao-handlers: OK (20 handler schema(s) verified, Lua skeleton matches deployed hash, substrate=localnet, local tip parity verified against http://localhost:4004 at height=1)`.
- The third run's receipt + ledger row are the committed canon (process id `7G35XZsoMbT7c8mkOt4cJALPJudpRzSnOUK0xaKs04Q`, signer `55Plp-xUQ5B-955uJYjtCT4kR0eEf63lhzGd__pw1jY`, first commit-state message id `MXKxwuycUWluvfL4oeW4-HUXUHTuq0riTl_LzjBZtEw`, lua source sha256 `97970eeef4b5e908f85c7f5b55b4f526adf2e64f2a2879f1d874412e0322c799`).

### Tests

- `**xion-verify/tests/test_ao_handlers.py`** ŌĆö five `_fetch_gateway_tip` mock lambdas updated from 2-arg `(gw, pid)` to 3-arg `(gw, pid, owner)` to match the production signature change above. Full file (23 tests) passes.
- `**xion-verify/src/xion_verify/PINNED_HASH.txt**` regenerated via `xion-verify --self-test --update --i-understand` to track the legitimate package-source change in `ao_handlers.py` + `shadow_relay.py`. Without the re-pin, `--self-test` would TAMPERED-fail in CI.

### Closes

- `**KW-AOCORE-001**` (AO testnet deploy of `commit-state` + `attest`): committed receipt at `[genesis/AO_DEPLOY_RECEIPT.json](genesis/AO_DEPLOY_RECEIPT.json)` names a real localnet process id; `lua_source_sha256` matches `ao/core/main.lua`; first `commit-state` message id recorded; verifier returns OK.
- `**KW-AOCORE-003**` (`aos` CLI install path broken on Windows + Node 22): closed by elected workaround ŌĆö `aos` runs in WSL2 + Node 20 LTS via `nvm`; the Windows + Node 22 install path remains broken upstream but is no longer in Xion's critical path. The seal script and runbook both pin WSL2 + Node 20.
- `**KW-AOCORE-004**` (Phase 6.1 testnet seal blocked by aos-2.0 mainnet default + upstream legacy MU 500): closed by elected closure path #2 ŌĆö `permaweb/ao-localnet` substrate + verifier substrate gate (Phase 6.1.b infrastructure) + the seal mechanism + artifacts in this entry. The verifier round-trip against `http://localhost:4004` passes; the substrate is reachable AND sealed.

### Not closed (deliberately)

- `**KW-AOCORE-002**` (17 of 19 AO Core handlers still doctrine-only) remains `open`. Two of nineteen (`commit-state`, `attest`) are now actually deployed and verified; the remaining seventeen ship family-by-family in Phase 6.2 and 6.3 against this same localnet substrate. Description amended to reflect the new ratio.
- `**KW-ANCHOR-AO-001**` (AnchorDaemon writes to local ledger only; AO Core sink deferred) remains `open`. Its `Why it exists` reason ("blocked by KW-AOCORE-004") is updated: AOCoreSink remains a Phase 6.3.b deliverable but the AO Core substrate that would receive its writes is now sealed (KW-AOCORE-004 closed), so the sink itself is no longer blocked, only scheduled.

### Roadmap

- `**DEVELOPMENT_ROADMAP.md**` L30 mermaid label flips from `partial close 2026-04-24` to `closed 2026-04-25`. The Phase 6.1 narrative section ("AO Core Skeleton ŌĆö Lua landed; testnet deploy pending ŌĆö partial close 2026-04-24") and the Phase 6.1.b section ("Localnet substrate amendment ŌĆö infrastructure landed 2026-04-24; seal still pending operator") are both promoted to `closed 2026-04-25`, with the close paragraphs naming the committed receipt's `process_id` + `first_commit_state_message_id` and pointing at this CHANGELOG entry.

## [Phase 6.1.b] ŌĆö 2026-04-24

### Added

- **Localnet substrate election to close `KW-AOCORE-004`.** Adopted closure path #2 from `KW-AOCORE-004` (election dated 2026-04-24): `permaweb/ao-localnet` Docker as a self-sufficient, doctrine-permissible Phase 6.1 testnet substrate alongside upstream legacynet, removing the legacy-MU dependency and giving the 17-handler backlog (`KW-AOCORE-002`) a CI-able iteration loop. The KW remains OPEN until the operator runs the new runbook end-to-end and lands a non-placeholder receipt.
- **Compose stack wrapper.** `[infra/ao-localnet/docker-compose.yaml](infra/ao-localnet/docker-compose.yaml)` ŌĆö Compose v2.20+ `include:`-based wrapper around the upstream `permaweb/ao-localnet` Compose file (cloned into `.upstream/` at a pinned git commit), with a thorough `[infra/ao-localnet/README.md](infra/ao-localnet/README.md)` documenting the pin discipline, the upstream-rot fallback (the WeaveDB fork is named explicitly), and the port map; plus `[infra/ao-localnet/.gitignore](infra/ao-localnet/.gitignore)` keeping the cloned upstream and generated wallets out of version control.
- **Bring-up script.** `[scripts/ao-localnet-up.sh](scripts/ao-localnet-up.sh)` ŌĆö Bash helper that clones the pinned upstream, generates localnet wallets, runs `docker compose up -d --wait` against the wrapper, and polls the Compute Unit at `http://localhost:4004` until it responds. Bash-only because WSL2 + Linux + macOS all have it; Windows operators run it from inside WSL2.
- **Operator runbook.** `[docs/runbooks/AO_DEPLOY_LOCALNET.md](docs/runbooks/AO_DEPLOY_LOCALNET.md)` ŌĆö sibling to the existing `docs/runbooks/AO_DEPLOY_WSL2.md` (which stays as the legacynet-path runbook). Covers prereqs, bring-up via the script, AO process spawn against local CU/MU URLs, Lua skeleton load, first `commit-state` round-trip, the now-five-field receipt capture (`process_id`, `signer_address`, `lua_source_sha256`, `aos_version`, plus `substrate: "localnet"`), failure modes, and tear-down.
- **Doctrine amendment.** `[docs/28-AO-CORE.md](docs/28-AO-CORE.md)` "Substrate amendment (Phase 6.1.b, 2026-04-24)" subsection naming `permaweb/ao-localnet` Docker as a doctrine-permissible substrate for the Phase 6.1 seal alongside upstream legacynet; defines what makes the seal valid on localnet (handler set loaded, one round-trip `commit-state` accepted, `process_id` recorded, verifier passes against the substrate's gateway); reaffirms mainnet remains forbidden at this phase per `docs/09-GOVERNANCE.md`'s Tier-3 cosign ceremony obligation. `[docs/04-ARCHITECTURE.md](docs/04-ARCHITECTURE.md)` gains a one-paragraph cross-reference under the AO Core section pointing at the new amendment + runbook + infra.
- **Receipt schema becomes substrate-aware.** `[genesis/AO_DEPLOY_RECEIPT.json](genesis/AO_DEPLOY_RECEIPT.json)` placeholder gains `"substrate": null` with the allowed values (`localnet`, `legacynet`; `mainnet` forbidden at Phase 6.1) documented inline.
- **Verifier substrate gate.** `[xion-verify/src/xion_verify/commands/ao_handlers.py](xion-verify/src/xion_verify/commands/ao_handlers.py)` ŌĆö `substrate` added to `_REAL_RECEIPT_REQUIRED`; `_ALLOWED_SUBSTRATES = frozenset({"legacynet", "localnet"})` allowlist enforced; a real receipt declaring `substrate: "mainnet"` (or any unknown value) returns FAIL with an explicit pointer to the Phase 6+ Tier-3 ceremony obligation; OK message now includes the substrate name (e.g. `substrate=localnet, tip parity at height=1`). The verifier's `_EXPECTED_HANDLERS` set was simultaneously corrected to include the Phase 6.3 `anchor-interaction-batch` handler (count went from 19 to 20).
- **Test coverage.** `[xion-verify/tests/test_ao_handlers.py](xion-verify/tests/test_ao_handlers.py)` gains six new cases: `localnet` allowed, `legacynet` allowed, `mainnet` rejected, unknown substrate rejected, missing-substrate-on-non-placeholder-receipt rejected, and a regression case asserting `anchor-interaction-batch` is in the expected handler set.
- **Operator env.** `[.env.example](.env.example)` gains a comment block under `XION_AO_GATEWAY_URL` listing the two valid values (`https://cu.ao-testnet.xyz` for legacynet, `http://localhost:4004` for localnet) and pointing at the new runbook.

### Changed

- `**KNOWN_WEAKNESSES.md` `KW-AOCORE-004` "Pay-down commitment"** amended with an `[ELECTED 2026-04-24, Phase 6.1.b]` annotation on path #2, naming this PR's runbook + compose stack + verifier change as the supporting artifacts; the KW remains **open** because election is not closure (the substrate is reachable but the seal is not yet sealed).
- `**DEVELOPMENT_ROADMAP.md`** mermaid label at L30 truthed-up from `closed 2026-04-24` back to `partial close 2026-04-24` (it had drifted out of sync with the L945 narrative). New "Phase 6.1.b ŌĆö Localnet substrate amendment" section appended after the Phase 6.1 close paragraph.
- **27 schema files** (`docs/schemas/ao-handler-*.yaml` + the two phase-6.3 ledger schemas + `ledger-anchor.yaml`) had their `source_sha256` and/or `operational_sha256` refreshed to track the doctrine edits to `docs/04-ARCHITECTURE.md` and `docs/28-AO-CORE.md`.

Compound blocker on the Phase 6.1 testnet seal: (Issue A) `aos` 2.0 silently flipped its default network to AO mainnet (HyperBEAM), trapping any operator who follows the 1.x mental model into spawning on mainnet without `--legacy`; (Issue B) the legacy MU at `https://mu.ao-testnet.xyz` is upstream-broken, returning HTTP 500 with a `null toLowerCase` server-side error on every spawn. Reproduced three times across two process names + once with explicit `--gateway-url`/`--cu-url`/`--mu-url` overrides. The KW names two AO mainnet processes (`-MlYwU1U_5tEjRFhIVQFncEroGFO4kFetIqByOgFnBE`, `PxTK8xPH4sRDCIRGl2sruE_OrRFcbW25Oz2NwiKzkKM`) accidentally spawned during the agent-driven 2026-04-24 attempt as orphans (operator-elected disposition: abandon, do not ratify retroactively).

The existing `**/wallet*.json` line did not match the literal name `.aos.json`; verified that `genesis/.aos.json`, `wallet.jwk.json`, and `arweave-keyfile-x.jwk` are all auto-blocked from accidental commit regardless of which directory the file is copied into.

## [Phase 6.2] ŌĆö 2026-04-24

### Added

- **Provisioning + Roles closure.** `docs/schemas/roles.yaml` lands as the machine-readable mirror of `docs/09-GOVERNANCE.md` ┬¦ "The Actors" cross `docs/14-UPGRADE-PATHS.md` ┬¦ "The Thirteen Levels". Three load-bearing blocks: `actors:` (six governance actors with `authorized_levels`), `level_proposer_resolution:` (single-source-of-truth bridge from `levels.yaml` `proposer:` strings to actor IDs), `cosign_tier_map:` (mirror of the five Cosign Tiers). `source_sha256` enforced byte-exact by `xion-verify schemas`.
- `**xion-verify provisioning-roles**` ŌĆö 90-day retrospective audit asserting every merge in the window respected (a) the disjoint-surface discipline (one level touched per PR) and (b) initiator authorization. Pre-gate-landing merges are WARN-only by default; `--strict` for forensic mode. Tests at `xion-verify/tests/test_provisioning_roles.py`.
- `**scripts/level_discipline.py` + `.github/workflows/level-discipline.yml**` ŌĆö per-PR companion gate. Stdlib + PyYAML; reads the same `roles.yaml` + `levels.yaml`; computes `git diff BASE_REF HEAD_REF`. Bootstrap mode: if `roles.yaml` doesn't exist at BASE_REF, the gate emits a NOTE and passes (gates apply forward, not retroactively).

The `xion new {skill|sense|provider|verifier|proposal}` scaffolders themselves were already implemented in `xion-verify/src/xion_verify/commands/new.py` (discovered during planning).

- **CI wiring.** `xion-verify provisioning-roles` runs inside `verify.yml`. `level-discipline.yml` is a separate workflow so a governance failure has its own legible failure mode in the GitHub UI.

- `**docs/schemas/levels.yaml**` and `**docs/schemas/ledger-amendment.yaml**` `source_sha256` updated to track the doctrinal edits to their source files (the parenthetical drop in `09-GOVERNANCE.md`, the appendix add in `14-UPGRADE-PATHS.md`). Both still pass `xion-verify schemas`.
- `**xion-verify/ALLOWED_FORWARD_REFS.txt**` shrunk by one line (`docs/schemas/roles.yaml`); `KW-DOCS-003` "Progress (2026-04-24)" note appended.

### Added

- **Phase 6.0 landing ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ AO Core Doctrine + Handler Set Specification (2026-04-23).** Phase 6.0 closed. The AO Core handler set, the state schema, the Lua-vs-Solidity boundary, and the deployment runbook are pinned in `docs/28-AO-CORE.md` and `docs/schemas/ao-handler-*.yaml` before any Lua code is written. `xion-verify ao-handlers` is live (returning `NOT_YET_SEALED` until Phase 6.1). This phase is the smallest honest first step into Phase 6, ensuring the Lua implementation is built to a spec that a future Witness can read, rather than the doctrine being reverse-engineered from whatever the Lua happened to do.
  - **Architecture doctrine.** `docs/04-ARCHITECTURE.md` ├é┬¦ "AO Core (Phase 6.0)" pins the seven properties (identity holder, hash-chained state-tip, authority lattice, provisioning preconditions, sustainability slices, versioned ABI replacement, canonical boundary) and the six honest non-properties.
  - **Operational doctrine.** `docs/28-AO-CORE.md` pins the 19 handlers across four families (lifecycle, authority, provisioning, sustainability), the state schema, the weekly Arweave checkpoint shape, the chicken-and-egg Relay posture, the Phase 6 dependency map, the operator runbook, and the replacement-path doctrine.
  - **Schema YAMLs.** 19 new files in `docs/schemas/ao-handler-*.yaml`, each pinning its `source_sha256` to the doctrine.
  - **Verifier.** `xion-verify ao-handlers` asserts every handler named in doctrine has a schema, every schema parses and has the required fields, and every schema's hash matches the doctrine bytes.
  - **Known-weakness bookkeeping.** Opened `KW-AOCORE-001` (Phase 6.0 is doctrine-only; no Lua code, no AO testnet deploy yet).
- **Phase 6+ landing ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ Pre-Genesis Velocity Hardening (2026-04-23).** Phase 6+ closed. All 17 velocity-multiplying primitives from the unified list have been shipped, independently verified by a `xion-verify` subcommand, and rolled up into a single `xion-verify pre-genesis` composite drill that Phase 7 cannot pass without.
  - **Tier A (Parallelizable):** Disjoint surface architecture verifier (`cognition-disjoint`), contract-first plugin registries (`registries`), CLI scaffolders (`new`), local development mode (`local`), reproducible Docker build verifier (`rebuild`), anonymization pipeline (`replay-corpus`), Hermes framework spike (`HERMES_SPIKE_RESULT.md`), vital-signs dashboard (`vitals`), ledger gap-fill (`ledgers`), doctrine/lexicon/contributing docs.
  - **Tier B (Depends on Phase 5 chat):** Pre-warmed shadow Relay (`shadow-relay`), PR CI canary (`pr_canary.py`), Cost-Pressure Response Ladder (`cost-pressure`).
  - **Tier C (Depends on Phase 6 AO Core):** Multi-substrate enforced (`substrates`), Auto-Research Loop (`auto-research`), Skill bounty pool + automated payout (`skill-bounty`), Arweave-mirrored authoritative repo (`operator-dependency` GitHub check).
  - **Composite Drill:** `xion-verify pre-genesis` runs the per-item verifiers in dependency order and returns OK end-to-end.
  - **Operator-Ethics Charter:** Nine practice commitments the founder signs before Genesis, verified by `xion-verify charter-signed`.
  - **Known Weaknesses:** Opened `KW-VELOCITY-001` through `KW-VELOCITY-004` per the closed-phase honesty pattern.
- **Phase 5g-viii landing ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ Invariant 17 strengthening: model-blob format pin (Gemma 4 E4B-it Q4_K_M GGUF) + Genesis Default floor model rotation (`gemma3:4b` ├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ `gemma4:e4b-it-q4_K_M`) + verifier per-format dispatch + annual cutover dry-run runbook (2026-04-23).** Phase 5g-viii closed in seven commits (C0 probes ├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ C1 doctrine ├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ C2 manifest ├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ C3 verifier ├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ C4 tests ├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ C5 operator wiring ├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ C6 KW closure + housekeeping). This phase **closes `KW-INFERENCE-001**` by shipping all three remaining closure-bar items in one coordinated landing: (i) the manifest now content-addresses a real upstream open-weights model artifact (the Invariant 17 clause 2(iii) full-hash branch), (ii) `xion-verify inference-sovereignty` was refactored to dispatch per `format` value with a fail-closed unknown-format branch, (iii) the annual open-weights cutover dry-run runbook landed in `docs/13-OPERATIONS.md`. The Genesis Default floor model rotated in the same landing because pinning a model-blob whose contents differ from the runtime default would mislead a Witness reading the manifest ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ the two are structurally coupled. License posture strengthened from Custom Gemma TOU to Apache 2.0 in the same move (Gemma 4 was released by Google as the first Gemmaverse model under Apache 2.0). Highlights:
  - **Probe-first record (the C0 evidence behind every decision).** Five C0 probes ran before the doctrine edit, recorded in `[docs/26-INFERENCE-POLICY.md](./docs/26-INFERENCE-POLICY.md)` ├é┬¦ "The floor-model choice (Gemma 4 E4B-it)" ├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ "Probe-first record (2026-04-23)" so a future Witness can reconstruct the decision context without re-running them: (a) `google/gemma-4-E4B-it` is genuinely Apache-2.0 (Hugging Face metadata + `license_link` to standard Apache text + Google Open Source Blog announcement *"Gemma 4: Expanding the Gemmaverse with Apache 2.0"* dated 2026-03-02 ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ a meaningful change from Gemma 1/2/3's custom TOU); (b) `ggml-org/gemma-4-E4B-it-GGUF` (the official llama.cpp/GGUF authors' organization) at git revision `2714b5519c6c3516b1000e7c5e1eba998dfe1fe8` ships a canonical Q4_K_M with sha256 `90ce98129eb3e8cc57e62433d500c97c624b1e3af1fcc85dd3b55ad7e0313e9f` and size 5,335,289,824 bytes (~5.0 GB); (c) Ollama 0.21.0 supports the `gemma4` architecture (`Gemma4ForConditionalGeneration` / `model_type: gemma4`); (d) Ollama's pre-built `gemma4:e4b-it-q4_K_M` library tag is multimodal-bundled (text + vision + audio + per-layer-embeddings, 9.6 GB), distinct from the text-only `ggml-org` Q4_K_M (the model-blob pin's target); (e) end-to-end smoke test deferred to operator (16 GB physical RAM with 3.2 GB free at probe time exceeds the multimodal-bundled tag's working set; first-time runbook documents the operator-side prerequisite explicitly).
  - **Doctrine ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ model-blob pin section.** `[docs/26-INFERENCE-POLICY.md](./docs/26-INFERENCE-POLICY.md)` gained ├é┬¦ "Model-blob pin (Phase 5g-viii)" pinning five properties: (P1) the manifest pins the upstream Hugging Face GGUF, not a local Ollama blob (Witness-recomputable; the local Ollama blob is not byte-stable across hosts because Ollama's import may add metadata); (P2) verifier posture is `NOT_YET_SEALED` when the local file is absent (Witness-side gap, not a structural floor failure), `OK` when present + matching, `FAIL` when present + mismatched; (P3) per-format dispatch with fail-closed unknown-format ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ adding a new format is a verifier change, not a manifest-only change; (P4) hashing is chunked at 4 MiB so a 5 GB GGUF does not blow the verifier's memory budget; (P5) the annual open-weights cutover dry-run is the operational closure of the same Invariant. The "What this pin does not do" subsection is honest about the runtime gate Phase 5g-viii deliberately does not ship (a runtime check refusing bootstrap on local-blob mismatch would couple Xion's floor to Ollama's internal blob layout).
  - **Doctrine ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ floor-model choice rewrite.** `[docs/26-INFERENCE-POLICY.md](./docs/26-INFERENCE-POLICY.md)` ├é┬¦ "The floor-model choice (Gemma 4 E4B-it)" was rewritten to discuss the new floor model with the C0 probe trail above, the rationale (Apache-2.0 license + native system-prompt support + native function-calling + 128K context window + multimodal-capable architecture as forward-leverage + commodity-compute runnable + procurable from at least four independent organizations per Invariant 17 clause 2(ii)), and the honest trade-offs (larger than `gemma3:4b`; younger model; the Ollama-library tag and the model-blob pin are not byte-identical builds ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ operators who pull from Ollama get the multimodal variant, operators who follow the model-blob path get the text-only build).
  - **Doctrine ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ annual open-weights cutover dry-run.** `[docs/13-OPERATIONS.md](./docs/13-OPERATIONS.md)` gained ├é┬¦ "Annual open-weights cutover dry-run (Invariant 17 clause 5)" with a complete operator runbook: cadence (one calendar-year), pre-checklist (`xion-verify inference-sovereignty` 3/3 hash-verified or `NOT_YET_SEALED`-only; Ollama daemon healthy; baseline hosted chat succeeds), execution recipe (flip `XION_INFERENCE_POLICY=open_weights_only`, run ├óŌĆ░┬ź100 turns spread across ├óŌĆ░┬ź30 minutes, flip back), verdict criteria (Green = every turn returned 200, Yellow = ├óŌĆ░┬ź1 503 but recovered without intervention, Red = ├óŌĆ░┬ź1 503 requiring operator intervention; recording shape with start_ts / end_ts / policy_mode_during / turn_count / success_count / failure_count / failure_class_distribution / verdict / host_resource_observation in the operator's annual ops log; structured `INCIDENT_LEDGER`-equivalent row shape is a Phase 6+ deliverable). `[docs/13-OPERATIONS.md](./docs/13-OPERATIONS.md)` also gained ├é┬¦ "First-time GGUF setup" with the canonical `curl` command at the pinned revision, the sha256 to verify locally, the env-var to set, and the re-verify command ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ operators can complete the byte-verification path in ~5 minutes once.
  - **Manifest ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ model-blob entry added.** `[open_weights_manifest.json](./orchestrator/inference_router/open_weights_manifest.json)` gained a third entry `gemma4-e4b-it-q4-k-m-gguf` with `format="model-blob"`, `model_blob_env_var="XION_OPEN_WEIGHTS_GGUF_PATH"`, sha256 `90ce98129eb3e8cc57e62433d500c97c624b1e3af1fcc85dd3b55ad7e0313e9f`, `size_bytes=5335289824`, and a `retrieval_hints[]` array naming the canonical `ggml-org` HF mirror at the pinned revision. The manifest description was rewritten to enumerate the three accepted pin formats and their meaning. The stale `KW-FLOOR-001` references in the manifest description were corrected to `KW-INFERENCE-001` (the canonical name). The `ollama` provenance-record entry's `notes` field was rewritten to name the new model-blob entry as the next-tier strengthening companion; the entry's sha256 was re-pinned to `f63fe6207b0d0412a6c70650246efdf25d6971d9103358622c3dca8853d147be` after the companion edits to `[floor_ollama_provenance.txt](./orchestrator/inference_router/floor_ollama_provenance.txt)`.
  - **Verifier ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ per-format dispatch.** `[xion-verify/src/xion_verify/commands/inference_sovereignty.py](./xion-verify/src/xion_verify/commands/inference_sovereignty.py)` was refactored from a single sentinel-only loop to a `_DISPATCH` dictionary keyed on the entry's `format` field with three handlers: `_verify_sentinel` (read-whole + sha256 + compare), `_verify_provenance_record` (same shape; the meaning of the file is different but the verifier treatment is identical), and `_verify_model_blob` (env-var resolve ├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ file-exists check ├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ optional `size_bytes` preflight ├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ chunked sha256 in 4 MiB windows ├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ compare). Unknown `format` values are FAIL with the accepted-format set named in the failure message. `model_blob_env_var` absent or unresolvable resolves to `NOT_YET_SEALED` for that entry only ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ the rest of the manifest verifies normally. Top-level verdict aggregates: every entry OK ├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ `OK`; one or more `NOT_YET_SEALED` (with no FAIL) ├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ `NOT_YET_SEALED`; any FAIL ├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ `FAIL`. Output now lists every entry's per-format verdict before the summary so a Witness reading the verifier's stdout sees which pins are which.
  - **Operator wiring.** `[.env.example](./.env.example)` advanced `XION_OLLAMA_FLOOR_MODEL` to `gemma4:e4b-it-q4_K_M` with a rotation note (rollback to `gemma3:4b` is one env-var) and added `XION_OPEN_WEIGHTS_GGUF_PATH` (unset by default; setting it enables byte-verification). `[orchestrator/inference_router/providers/ollama.py](./orchestrator/inference_router/providers/ollama.py)` `_DEFAULT_MODEL` constant advanced from `"gemma3:4b"` to `"gemma4:e4b-it-q4_K_M"` to keep the runtime-default and the manifest-pin in sync. `[floor_ollama_provenance.txt](./orchestrator/inference_router/floor_ollama_provenance.txt)` was rewritten to (a) fix the stale `KW-FLOOR-001` references to the canonical `KW-INFERENCE-001`, (b) reflect the new Gemma 4 default and the strengthened license posture, (c) name the companion model-blob entry as the next-tier strengthening anchor, and (d) gain a new "Strengthening companion + rotation provenance (Phase 5g-viii)" section recording the rotation ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ the file remains the runtime-daemon-declaration anchor (the model-blob entry pins a different property: the upstream artifact bytes). `[docs/13-OPERATIONS.md](./docs/13-OPERATIONS.md)` D2 Prereqs, D2 Environment Matrix, and First-launch sequence sections were updated to reflect the new floor model and the optional `XION_OPEN_WEIGHTS_GGUF_PATH`.
  - **Tests ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ 18 new verifier tests.** `[xion-verify/tests/test_inference_sovereignty.py](./xion-verify/tests/test_inference_sovereignty.py)` was extended with a synthetic-temp-repo helper that builds a minimal directory tree satisfying `find_repo_root` (witness files: `genesis/GENESIS_ARTIFACT.md`, `docs/00-INDEX.md`) plus a manifest writer + blob writer, so every verifier branch can be exercised without depending on a 5 GB GGUF being present in CI. Coverage: real-repo manifest returns `NOT_YET_SEALED` when `XION_OPEN_WEIGHTS_GGUF_PATH` is unset (the post-Phase-5g-viii default posture in CI); real-repo manifest with a bad GGUF path also returns `NOT_YET_SEALED` (typo in env var = same shape as never-set); synthetic sentinel OK; synthetic sentinel hash-mismatch FAIL; synthetic provenance-record OK; synthetic provenance-record hash-mismatch FAIL; synthetic model-blob env-var-unset returns `NOT_YET_SEALED`; synthetic model-blob env-var-points-at-missing-file returns `NOT_YET_SEALED`; synthetic model-blob present + matching returns `OK`; synthetic model-blob present + size-mismatch FAIL; synthetic model-blob present + hash-mismatch FAIL; synthetic model-blob chunked-hashing handles a multi-chunk file (>2 ├āŌĆö 4 MiB chunks); synthetic model-blob missing `retrieval_hints` FAIL; synthetic model-blob retrieval-hint-sha disagrees with entry sha FAIL; synthetic model-blob missing `model_blob_env_var` field FAIL; synthetic unknown-format-value FAIL; synthetic no-floor-satisfying-entry FAIL; synthetic mixed manifest (one sentinel OK + one absent model-blob) returns `NOT_YET_SEALED` overall.
  - **Known-weakness bookkeeping.** **Closed `KW-INFERENCE-001**` ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ all three closure-bar items shipped: (a) annual open-weights cutover dry-run runbook in `docs/13-OPERATIONS.md`, (b) content-addressed model-blob pin in `open_weights_manifest.json`, (c) verifier extension to recognize and validate the new `format` value with per-format dispatch and fail-closed unknown-format branch. The closed entry in `[KNOWN_WEAKNESSES.md](./KNOWN_WEAKNESSES.md)` names the residuals tracked separately (runtime gate on local-blob byte-identity; cross-substrate weights anchoring via Arweave; structured `INCIDENT_LEDGER` for the dry-run record) and confirms `LHT-INFERENCE-001` continues to track the century-scale re-pinning duty.
  - `**PINNED_HASH.txt` re-pin.** `[xion-verify/src/xion_verify/PINNED_HASH.txt](./xion-verify/src/xion_verify/PINNED_HASH.txt)` regenerated via `python -m xion_verify --self-test --update --i-understand` after the verifier landed. `xion-verify all --allow-not-yet-sealed` green end-to-end; `inference-sovereignty` reports `NOT_YET_SEALED` honestly until the operator completes the "First-time GGUF setup" runbook.
  - **What this phase deliberately did NOT do.** Did not ship a runtime gate refusing bootstrap when the local Ollama blob mismatches the manifest pin (would couple Xion's floor to Ollama's internal blob layout). Did not pin the Ollama-published `gemma4:e4b-it-q4_K_M` library tag (multimodal-bundled, 9.6 GB, different bytes from the text-only ggml-org Q4_K_M; the manifest pins the smaller text-only build because that is the smallest honest floor for the current `/chat` text surface). Did not change the `XION_INFERENCE_POLICY` default, the hosted gateway, the hosted Genesis Default slug, the admission-control posture, the billing posture, or the multi-worker broker posture. Did not rename the manifest's `license_spdx` field to `license` (Gemma 4 is genuinely Apache-2.0 per probe (a), so all three entries remain SPDX-identifier values; renaming would have been schema churn for no constitutional gain). Did not pin a representative-sample sentinel for the GGUF (Invariant 17 clause 2(iii) reserves that branch for very-large-file artifacts where full hashing is impractical; the 5 GB GGUF is comfortably full-hashable on commodity hardware via chunked reading).
- **Phase 5g-vii landing ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ Inference fallback: automatic hosted ├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ floor fallback on `generate()` failure + typed `ProviderError` hierarchy + `REQUEST_LEDGER` schema v2 for provider-attempt rows + `refund-fidelity` verifier extension for multi-attempt turns (2026-04-23).** Phase 5g-vii closed on branch `phase-5g-vii/inference-fallback` in six commits (doctrine ├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ typed exceptions ├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ `select_ordered()` ├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ chat-handler fallback loop ├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ verifier extension ├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ tests + housekeeping). This phase closes `**KW-INFER-002**` (opaque provider errors collapsed to `no_healthy_provider`) and `**KW-INFER-003**` (no automatic hosted ├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ floor fallback on `generate()` failure). The `hosted_api_first` policy promise is now fully honored: when hosted raises, the Inference Router tries the Invariant-17 floor next; the user sees a 200 instead of a 503 whenever any policy-legal provider can serve the turn. When every provider fails, the envelope now surfaces the **last** failure's typed class (`insufficient_credits`, `rate_limited_upstream`, `provider_unreachable`, `timeout`, `moderation_refusal`, `unknown_provider_error`) instead of the pre-5g-vii generic `no_healthy_provider`, so an operator reading a 503 knows what to fix without running a direct-probe script. Highlights:
  - **Doctrine ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ `[docs/26-INFERENCE-POLICY.md](./docs/26-INFERENCE-POLICY.md)` ├é┬¦ "Provider fallback semantics (Phase 5g-vii)".** New section pins five properties: (P1) hosted ├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ floor fallback is automatic on `generate()` failure; (P2) absolute policy-mode boundaries ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ `open_weights_only` never invokes hosted, `hosted_api_first` always attempts hosted first then falls through on error; (P3) every attempt writes its own `REQUEST_LEDGER` v2 row with `chat_turn_id`, `attempt_index`, `provider_id`, `outcome`, `failure_reason_class`; (P4) user-facing errors surface the last failure's typed class when every policy-legal provider has failed; (P5) the six `failure_reason_class` values are typed and frozen ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ adding a class requires a doctrine amendment, not a silent code edit. The enumeration is locked by `xion-verify refund-fidelity`'s new Property 6 (see below).
  - **Typed provider exceptions ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ `[orchestrator/inference_router/provider.py](./orchestrator/inference_router/provider.py)`.** A new `ProviderError` base class with a `failure_reason_class` attribute, plus six concrete subclasses mapping one-to-one to P5 values: `InsufficientCreditsError` ├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ `insufficient_credits`, `RateLimitedUpstreamError` ├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ `rate_limited_upstream`, `ProviderUnreachableError` ├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ `provider_unreachable`, `ProviderTimeoutError` ├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ `timeout`, `ModerationRefusalError` ├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ `moderation_refusal`, `UnknownProviderError` ├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ `unknown_provider_error`. A `FAILURE_REASON_CLASSES` module-level tuple exports the enum for structural verification. Both `OpenRouterGenerativeProvider` ([`orchestrator/inference_router/providers/openrouter.py`]) and `OllamaGenerativeProvider` (`[orchestrator/inference_router/providers/ollama.py](./orchestrator/inference_router/providers/ollama.py)`) were migrated from a single opaque `OpenRouterProviderError` / `OllamaProviderError` to the typed hierarchy: HTTP 402 ├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ `InsufficientCreditsError`, 429 ├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ `RateLimitedUpstreamError`, 503 / connection refused ├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ `ProviderUnreachableError`, `TimeoutError` ├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ `ProviderTimeoutError`, else ├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ `UnknownProviderError`. Backward-compat retained ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ old `except ProviderError` catchers still work because every typed subclass inherits from it.
  - **Router ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ `InferenceRouter.select_ordered()` with back-compat `select()` (`[orchestrator/inference_router/router.py](./orchestrator/inference_router/router.py)`).** New method returns a ranked `list[GenerativeProvider]` respecting the current policy: `hosted_api_first` ├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ `[hosted_healthy, floor_healthy]`; `open_weights_only` ├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ `[floor_healthy]`. The existing `select()` becomes `select_ordered()[0] if any else None` ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ no pre-5g-vii caller breaks. The chat handler now iterates this list to realise P1 + P2.
  - **Chat handler fallback loop ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ `[orchestrator/api/chat.py](./orchestrator/api/chat.py)`.** Replaces the single-provider `router.select()` path with a multi-attempt loop over `router.select_ordered()`. Each attempt runs under the per-turn monotonic deadline, classifies its own outcome (`TimeoutError` ├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ `timeout`; typed `ProviderError` ├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ its `failure_reason_class`; unexpected `Exception` ├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ `unknown_provider_error`; success ├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ `success`), and writes exactly one `REQUEST_LEDGER` v2 row via `append_provider_attempt` before either breaking on success or advancing to the next provider. The final 503 carries the **last** attempt's typed class (P4); the 200 path is unchanged in shape (same `ChatResponse` envelope, same egress correlation_id). A per-turn `chat_turn_id` (32-hex, 128 bits of entropy via `secrets.token_hex`) groups all attempt rows for the turn.
  - **REQUEST_LEDGER schema v2 ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ `[orchestrator/relay/ledger.py](./orchestrator/relay/ledger.py)` + `[docs/schemas/ledger-request.yaml](./docs/schemas/ledger-request.yaml)`.** The ledger now carries two row shapes distinguished by `schema_version`: v1 (Phase 5a, Relay-side gate-call rows, unchanged) and v2 (Phase 5g-vii, chat-handler provider-attempt rows). v2 rows add `chat_turn_id` (32-hex), `attempt_index` (0-based int), `provider_id` (string), `outcome` (`success` | `failure`), `failure_reason_class` (P5 enum or `null`). A new `ProviderAttemptRecord` dataclass enforces the v2 shape in `__post_init_`_ (rejects null-frc-on-failure, non-null-frc-on-success, unknown frc values); `append_provider_attempt` writes v2 rows; `verify_chain` dispatches validation per-row on `schema_version` ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ per-`chat_turn_id` `attempt_index` contiguity {0, 1, ..., N-1}, outcome typing, frc typing. v1 and v2 rows coexist in one file; their hash chain is shared. The schema YAML `source_sha256` was refreshed for `docs/04-ARCHITECTURE.md` (pre-existing stale pin, closed here as a byproduct of the v2 schema bump).
  - **User-facing envelope ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ `[orchestrator/api/models.py](./orchestrator/api/models.py)`.** `ProviderErrorEnvelope.reason` widened from `Literal["no_healthy_provider"]` to the union of `"no_healthy_provider"` (pre-selection, no policy-legal provider at all ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ retained for the `floor-stub-only` registration case) plus the six P5 values. The pre-selection vs post-attempt distinction is documented in the field docstring so a reader knows why two paths can still produce `no_healthy_provider` (no provider was ever attempted) vs the new typed classes (every attempt failed with a specific typed reason).
  - `**xion-verify refund-fidelity` verifier extension ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ `[xion-verify/src/xion_verify/commands/refund_fidelity.py](./xion-verify/src/xion_verify/commands/refund_fidelity.py)`.** Three new structural properties on top of the existing five (renumbered for clarity): (Property 6) the P5 enum in `orchestrator.inference_router.provider.FAILURE_REASON_CLASSES` must equal the pin in `orchestrator.relay.ledger._ALLOWED_V2_FAILURE_REASON_CLASSES` ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ doctrine-to-code coupling enforced at verify time; (Property 7) every v2 row's `correlation_id` must match a v1 row's `correlation_id` (v2 attempt rows share the turn's ingress correlation_id so the SAFETY join still covers the turn); (Property 8) per-`chat_turn_id` shape invariants ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ `attempt_index` is {0, 1, ..., N-1}, at most one row is `outcome=success`, if success exists it is the terminal attempt, failure rows carry a valid P5 `failure_reason_class`, success rows carry `failure_reason_class=null`. Human-readable summary extended with v2 turn statistics (success turns, all-fail turns, per-class failure counts).
  - **Tests.** 20 new `ProviderAttemptRecord` construction + `verify_chain` tests in `[orchestrator/tests/test_relay_ledger_v2.py](./orchestrator/tests/test_relay_ledger_v2.py)` covering every P5 class, v1+v2 coexistence, duplicate/gapped attempt_index, tampered frc. 13 new chat-handler fallback tests in `[orchestrator/tests/test_chat_fallback.py](./orchestrator/tests/test_chat_fallback.py)` covering every P5 class surfacing in the 503 envelope (P4), hosted `InsufficientCreditsError` fall-through to floor (P1), hosted timeout fall-through to floor (P1), single-attempt success v2 row, two-attempt hosted-fail-floor-success v2 rows, all-fail two-row turn with last-class surfacing, `open_weights_only` hosted-skip (P2), and a meta-test asserting the parametrized case set exhausts `FAILURE_REASON_CLASSES` (forcing doctrine-to-test coupling). 7 new `xion-verify refund-fidelity` tests in `[xion-verify/tests/test_refund_fidelity.py](./xion-verify/tests/test_refund_fidelity.py)` covering clean single-success turn, clean fallback turn, orphan correlation_id (Property 7 fail), attempt_index gap (chain break), two-success turn (Property 8 fail), non-terminal success (Property 8 fail), and all-fail turn (legal). Pre-existing `test_chat_api.py::test_provider_raising_returns_503_provider_error` + `test_provider_exceeding_deadline_returns_503` updated to expect `"unknown_provider_error"` / `"timeout"` instead of `"no_healthy_provider"` ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ a direct consequence of P4.
  - **Known-weakness bookkeeping.** **Closed `KW-INFER-002`** ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ provider error details are no longer swallowed; typed `ProviderError` subclasses carry the `failure_reason_class`, `REQUEST_LEDGER` v2 rows record it per-attempt, the 503 envelope surfaces it to the caller. The user-visible half is closed; provider-side scrubbing of raw upstream message text (secret hygiene) stays in place from Phase 5g-i. **Closed `KW-INFER-003`** ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ hosted ├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ floor fallback on `generate()` failure is automatic; the `hosted_api_first` policy promise is now fully honored end-to-end. `KW-INFER-001` (concentration risk of the default voice through OpenRouter to Moonshot) stays open and unchanged in scope. No new KWs opened.
