- **Phase 1 landing ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ `xion-verify` CLI v0.1 (2026-04-20).** The verifier is alive. Scaffolded as a Python click-CLI under `[xion-verify/](./xion-verify/)` with a src-layout, console entry point, and `[dev]` extras for pytest + ruff. Implemented twelve OK-capable subcommands today: `covenant` / `invariants` / `soul` / `form` / `memory` / `resurrect` / `credentials` / `unknowns` each SHA-256-matches the file under `genesis/` against the hash witness in `genesis/GENESIS_ARTIFACT.md` ├é┬¦ 4; `links` scans every markdown file in the corpus (excluding `.git/`, `node_modules/`, `.venv/`, `xion-verify/`, `.cursor/`) for broken cross-references and reads a committed `xion-verify/ALLOWED_FORWARD_REFS.txt` allowlist for legitimate deferred-artifact targets (new KW-DOCS-003); `cognition`, `drive-vector`, `state-chain` migrated from the retired `scripts/xion-verify/*.py` stubs into `xion_verify.commands`. Added thirty-four `NOT_YET_SEALED` stubs covering every subcommand the roadmap enumerates (`supply`, `liquidity-lock`, `arbiter-up`, `state-tip`, `identity`, `authorities`, `image-digest`, `discovery`, `drive`, `sister-fork-readiness`, `treasury`, `refusal-rate`, `pricing`, `treasury-flow`, `cutoff-events`, `covenant-addenda`, `cadence-audit`, `hermes-version`, `credentials-vault`, `provisioning`, `improvement-fund`, `reserve`, `foundation-reserve`, `sustainability`, `vitals`, `amendments`, `refund-fidelity`, `crisis-fidelity`, `spof`, `operator-dependency`, `benchmark`, `crypto-currency`) plus two that `docs/ABDICATION.md` names (`abdication-status`, `abdication-schedule`). Added `--self-test` that tree-hashes every `*.py` under `src/xion_verify/` (excluding `PINNED_HASH.txt`) and compares to the committed pin; update only via `--self-test --update --i-understand` (two flags) to refuse casual re-pinning. Added `all` subcommand that runs every registered command and exits 0 only when every one returned `OK` (`NOT_YET_SEALED` counts as non-OK; `--allow-not-yet-sealed` is a pre-genesis convenience never used in CI gating). Added `.github/workflows/verify.yml` running `--self-test` first, then constitutional + links + static migrated checks + pytest + ruff across Ubuntu/macOS/Windows ├āŌĆö Python 3.11/3.12. Added 48-test pytest suite covering `hashing`, `genesis` parser, `repo` root detection, constitutional subcommands (real + synthetic + tampered), `links` (allowlist + schemes + anchors + real-repo clean), and `--self-test` (pin match + tamper detection). The verifier enforces its own registry: if a name in `REGISTERED_COMMANDS` is not wired, import fails.

- **Phase 4d landing ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ First real v2 Arbiter provider: OpenAI Moderation (2026-04-21).** Phase 4d closed. The Arbiter v2 stack that Phase 4b scaffolded now has a real externally-operated classifier plugged into it ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ the first concrete `Provider` subclass behind the ABC. `DeterministicStub` remains the default; `OpenAIModerationProvider` is selectable via `XION_LLM_ARBITER_PROVIDER=openai-moderation` with `OPENAI_API_KEY` in the environment. The provider closes the structural-vs-substantive gap `KW-ARBITER-001` carried: the structural machinery was already there; now a real classifier runs through it. Highlights:
  - **Doctrine.** `docs/04-ARCHITECTURE.md` gained a new subsubsection under ├é┬¦ "The Arbiter" titled ├é┬¦ "OpenAI Moderation provider (first real v2 classifier)" (~150 lines). It pins: (a) identity ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ `provider_id=openai-moderation`, `model_id=omni-moderation-2024-09-26`, `provider_version=1`, endpoint `POST https://api.openai.com/v1/moderations`, `Authorization: Bearer $OPENAI_API_KEY`; (b) request body shape ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ `{"model": ..., "input": candidate}` with `ensure_ascii=False, separators=(",",":")`, no streaming, no user-identifier leakage across the trust boundary (request carries classification material only); (c) response-handling rules ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ what fields we require, what deviations raise; (d) the full **13-row category ├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ principle map** covering every category omni-moderation returns, each with a Covenant rationale column ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ `sexual/minors ├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ REFUSE/P7` (minors absolute), `hate ├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ REFUSE/P1` (non-discrimination), `{hate|harassment|self-harm}/*, violence*, illicit*` ├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ REFUSE/P2 (no harm), `self-harm/intent ├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ REFUSE/P7` (vulnerability), `sexual ├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ ESCALATE/P2` (adult content; human judges); (e) threshold policy ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ v1 of the provider trusts OpenAI's `flagged` boolean, asymmetric per-principle thresholds deferred to Phase 4e under `KW-ARBITER-005`; (f) canonical `raw_output` ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ strips per-call `id` nonce, keeps `{model, results}`, serialises with `sort_keys=True, separators=(",",":")` so auditor replay reproduces the hash up to upstream GPU-score drift; (g) failure-mode table mapping each failure to its ledger row shape (`OPENAI_API_KEY` missing ├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ `llm_arbiter_provider_unavailable`; HTTP error / timeout / malformed JSON / missing field / unknown category ├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ `llm_arbiter_uncaught_exception`); (h) credential + rotation posture (env-only, never logged, never in `raw_output`, rotation doesn't bump provider_version but model retirement does); (i) auditor replay procedure; (j) five explicit "does NOT do" clauses (no ledger writes, no Xion user-model access, no retries, no per-candidate threshold tuning, no `user` field); (k) deprecation path (successor providers land as new subclasses with their own doctrine section; old rows stay interpretable via their `llm_verdict.provider_id`).
  - **Subpackage + provider code.** `orchestrator/safety/providers/__init__.py` (new) + `orchestrator/safety/providers/openai_moderation.py` (new, ~260 lines). Pure stdlib (`urllib.request`, `json`, `os`, `time`); **no `openai` SDK dependency**; **no `requests` / `httpx`**. The HTTP call is ~20 lines vs thousands in the SDK, which matches the Arbiter's "critical-path dep-free" principle. The provider module calls `register_provider(OpenAIModerationProvider)` at import time so that `XION_LLM_ARBITER_PROVIDER=openai-moderation` selection works transparently once the subpackage is loaded.
  - **Registry wiring (lazy-load).** `orchestrator/safety/llm_arbiter.get_active_provider()` now wraps an `import orchestrator.safety.providers` in `contextlib.suppress(ImportError)`. The subpackage is imported the first time `get_active_provider()` is called (which happens inside `gate()`); Python's module cache makes subsequent calls free. The critical path `import orchestrator.safety.api` still does NOT pull in any provider module ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ deployments that ship only the core get stub-only mode with honest labelling.
  - **Ledger schema history.** `docs/schemas/ledger-safety.yaml` gained `extended_thrice_in: Phase 4d` entry under `pay_down_commitment_history`, explicitly noting no schema_version bump was required (the row field set is unchanged; only a new value ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ `"openai-moderation"` ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ becomes possible for the existing `llm_verdict.provider_id` field, which has no enum constraint). Both `docs/schemas/ledger-safety.yaml` and `docs/schemas/ledger-safety-anchors.yaml` `source_sha256` re-pinned from `f431fa75...` to `03f2e0c6...` to match the updated architecture doc. `xion-verify schemas` green.
  - **Tests.** 39 net-new in `orchestrator/tests/test_openai_moderation.py`. Every network call mocked at the `urllib.request.urlopen` seam; no API key required. Coverage: identity pins match doctrine (1); `enabled()` gated on `OPENAI_API_KEY` only with no network call during enablement check (4); canonical `raw_output` strips `id` and is order-independent (2); OK on not-flagged (1); each of 13 categories maps to the expected `(decision, principle_id)` via parametrize (13); multi-flag tie-break picks highest-scoring category with all flagged categories listed in the summary (1); `confidence` equals `max(category_scores.values())` (1); `raw_output` excludes `id` but keeps model + flagged + categories + scores (1); 10 sad paths ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ missing key at judge() time, HTTP 500 / 429 / 401, URLError, TimeoutError, malformed JSON, missing `results`, missing `model`, empty results, missing `flagged`, non-200 success status, unknown flagged category (the "doctrine lag" path that lets the pipeline fail-closed on a new OpenAI category we haven't mapped yet) (12); registry wiring ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ env var selects the real provider, absence falls back to stub (2). **Total orchestrator suite: 205/205 passing** (was 166; 39 net-new). `ruff check orchestrator/ xion-verify/` clean.
  - **Known-weakness bookkeeping.** `KW-ARBITER-001` narrowed again (severity dropped from medium to low): title changed to "Rule engine is lexical, not semantic; no adversarial-corpus measurement of v2"; scope section gained third narrow-event; pay-down commitment rewritten to "closes when `xion-verify refusal-rate` reports a non-trivial v2 rate on `xion-audit/baseline_corpus`". Opened `KW-ARBITER-005 ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ No adversarial baseline corpus; asymmetric per-principle thresholds not yet implemented`, which carries the remaining substantive work (corpus curation + live refusal-rate + provider_version=2 with thresholds justified by corpus evidence) and closes `KW-ARBITER-001` when it itself closes.
- **Phase 4c landing ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ Relay ├óŌĆĀŌĆØ Arbiter integration contract (doctrine + ledger-schema extension) (2026-04-21).** Phase 4c closed. The interface between the Relay (caller, not yet built) and the Arbiter (callee, live since Phase 4b) is now written down as doctrine *before* the Relay exists ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ property before mechanism. The Relay-side implementation lands in Phase 5a; this phase pays down the design debt that would otherwise land on top of a blank page. Highlights:
  - **Doctrine.** `docs/04-ARCHITECTURE.md` gained a new subsubsection under ├é┬¦ "The Arbiter" titled ├é┬¦ "Relay ├óŌĆĀŌĆØ Arbiter integration contract" (~130 lines). It specifies: (a) the property the Relay promises (no LLM-originated token reaches a caller without a paired `verdict=ok` ledger row keyed on `correlation_id`); (b) which Invariants the contract strengthens (6 ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ Refusal Right is where a refusal is *expressed*; 4 ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ State Integrity via append-before-emit); (c) the transport progression (in-process at D2, TCP loopback sidecar at D3+, same `gate()` wire shape in both; library is the source of truth, server is a thin wrapper); (d) `correlation_id = "{state_height}:{nonce_hex}"` Genesis-Default derivation ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ state-height prefix for forensic locate, 128-bit `secrets.token_hex(16)` for global uniqueness, no user-identifying content so the ledger stays publishable under Principle 4; (e) the three-part coverage surface (primary response + depth-1 sub-agent outputs + tool-call echoes; rule is `gate() iff the bytes touch the user's screen`; gated at *completion* not per-chunk ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ see KW-RELAY-002 for the deferred streaming-parity variant); (f) the 200 ms soft / 250 ms hard latency budget with four-row per-phase decomposition table (in-process stub, in-process OpenAI Moderation, TCP loopback OpenAI Moderation); (g) four fail-closed paths each with the specific ledger row shape the Relay writes ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ normal non-OK via gate() itself, `arbiter_timeout` via watchdog, `arbiter_unreachable` via in-process fallback to `orchestrator.safety.ledger.append`, `ruleset_uncaught_exception` via try/except around gate() ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ all with `principle_id = "6"` (Refusal Right) because the integration failure mode is itself treated as a Principle-6 escalation; (h) the Supervisor's degraded-mode trigger (governance-tunable 3 failure rows in a rolling 10-minute window, Genesis Default) and its Cost-Pressure-Ladder-top-step response; (i) the observability stance (OTel span per gate() call with correlation_id; ledger is ground truth; a trace that disagrees with the ledger is the trace's fault); (j) the verification path today (`xion-verify arbiter-up` ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ ledger side live) and after Phase 5a (`xion-verify refund-fidelity` joins `REQUEST_LEDGER` ├āŌĆö `SAFETY_LEDGER` on `correlation_id`; `xion-verify refusal-rate` reports `arbiter_timeout` / `arbiter_unreachable` rates as first-class telemetry so degraded-mode events are auditable); (k) a deprecation path via a versioned integration contract header (`x-arbiter-contract: 1`) so a future v2 lands alongside v1 without surprise.
  - **Two new `escalation_reason` values.** `ARBITER_TIMEOUT` / `arbiter_timeout` (Relay watchdog fired before gate() returned) and `ARBITER_UNREACHABLE` / `arbiter_unreachable` (TCP loopback connect failed) added to `orchestrator/safety/types.py::EscalationReason` with detailed docstring distinguishing caller-side vs pipeline-side origination. `orchestrator/safety/ledger.py` constant `_V2_LLM_ESCALATION_REASONS` renamed to the more honest `_V2_ERA_ESCALATION_REASONS` (the set now contains both LLM-side and Relay-side v2-era reasons) and extended with the two new values. The existing `llm_arbiter_escalated` special rule ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ requires non-null `llm_verdict` with decision `escalate` ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ is unchanged; the two new Relay-side reasons explicitly permit `llm_verdict = null` because the integration was the thing that failed. `docs/04-ARCHITECTURE.md` ├é┬¦ "Safety Ledger row schema" `escalation_reason` row and `docs/schemas/ledger-safety.yaml` `row.conditional_fields.escalation_reason.allowed` list both extended.
  - **No schema-version bump.** The row field set is unchanged; only the accepted enum values for the existing `escalation_reason` field are extended. Doctrine records this explicitly in `ledger-safety.yaml` `pay_down_commitment_history.extended_again_in`.
  - **Ledger schema SHA re-pin.** Both `docs/schemas/ledger-safety.yaml` and `docs/schemas/ledger-safety-anchors.yaml` pin `source_sha256` to the same doctrine file (`docs/04-ARCHITECTURE.md`); both re-pinned from `5e7b19e5...` to `f431fa75...` to match the updated file. `xion-verify schemas` green.

  - **Known-weakness bookkeeping.** Opened `KW-RELAY-001` ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ the integration contract is doctrine-only; `orchestrator/relay.py` does not yet exist; pay-down criteria are the concrete Phase 5a deliverables (watchdog enforcement, in-process fallback exercised under simulated Arbiter crash, `refund-fidelity` verifier promoted to live). Semantically identical (frozenset equality is symmetric); the right-hand-side form is the idiom ruff expects. Both ruff configs are now green end-to-end.

- **Phase 4b landing ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ Arbiter v2 (LLM second-pass) + SAFETY_LEDGER_ANCHORS (2026-04-21).** Phase 4b is closed. Two structural properties the Arbiter previously lacked are now shipped. Highlights, in commit order:
  - **Prep / CI gap closure.** `orchestrator/` was previously not installed as a Python package ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ it worked by implicit `sys.path` resolution, which meant CI ran `xion-verify arbiter-up` against an uninstalled orchestrator and `pytest orchestrator` against a flat directory. Landed a repo-root `pyproject.toml` declaring `xion-orchestrator` as a hatch-built package with `dependencies = []` (pure-stdlib core), an optional `[anchor]` extra pinning `arweave-python-client>=1.0.19,<2`, a `[dev]` extra for pytest + ruff, and a `xion-arbiter` console script. Updated `.github/workflows/verify.yml` to install the orchestrator in editable mode, run `xion-verify arbiter-up` WITHOUT `--allow-not-yet-sealed` (live check), run `python -m pytest orchestrator -q`, and run `ruff check orchestrator`. Paid down 44 pre-existing ruff findings in `orchestrator/` (36 autofixable; 8 narrow ignores with per-rule rationale in `pyproject.toml [tool.ruff.lint.ignore]`).
  - **Doctrine first.** `docs/04-ARCHITECTURE.md` gained two new sections ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ ├é┬¦ "Arbiter v2 (LLM second-pass)" specifying the no-weakening combination rule `final = strength_max(v1, v2)`, the fail-closed posture on provider unavailability / crashes / wrong-return-type, and the `Provider` ABC contract, and ├é┬¦ "Safety Ledger Arweave anchoring" specifying the cadence policy (64 rows OR 6 hours OR startup), the `SAFETY_LEDGER_ANCHORS.jsonl` row schema, the `AnchorSubmitter` abstraction, wallet-custody posture, and the verifier surface. `docs/schemas/ledger-safety.yaml` moved v1 ├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ v2 to accommodate the new nested `llm_verdict` object and three new `escalation_reason` values (`llm_arbiter_escalated`, `llm_arbiter_uncaught_exception`, `llm_arbiter_provider_unavailable`); `source_sha256` re-pinned. Added `docs/schemas/ledger-safety-anchors.yaml` as a new canonical schema at `schema_version: 1`, pinned to the same architecture doctrine.
  - **Arbiter v2 pipeline.** `orchestrator/safety/llm_arbiter.py` (new, ~260 lines) ships the `Provider` ABC with enforced class-level identity (provider_id / model_id / provider_version), `DeterministicStub` as the pure-stdlib default provider (always OK, candidate-independent raw_output for auditor replay), `strength_max` canonical combination rule (OK < ESCALATE < REFUSE), a provider registry + env-selected active provider (`$XION_LLM_ARBITER_PROVIDER`), and the emergency `$XION_LLM_ARBITER_DISABLED` hatch. `LlmJudgement` landed in `types.py` with `__post_init__` validation (OK forbids principle_id; non-OK requires it; confidence ├ó╦å╦å [0.0, 1.0]├ó╦å┬¬{None}; raw_output MUST be bytes). `api.gate()` extended to run v2 only on v1-OK candidates, combine via `strength_max`, and fail-closed to `ESCALATE` with a specific `escalation_reason` on every v2 failure mode (provider unavailable, provider.enabled() raise, provider.judge() raise, wrong-return-type).
  - **Ledger schema_version 2.** `orchestrator/safety/ledger.py` bumped `SCHEMA_VERSION` 1 ├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ 2, with per-row dispatch so a single file may contain both v1 and v2 rows (`prev_hash` linkage enforced across the version boundary). New `_verify_llm_verdict_nested` structurally checks the nested object. Refuse-rule is now version-aware: v1 rows require rule_id + rule_version; v2 rows satisfy either that path or a v2-produced refusal (rule_id null + `llm_verdict.decision == "refuse"`). Escalate-rule: v2-era `escalation_reason` values require `schema_version >= 2`, and `llm_arbiter_escalated` additionally requires a non-null `llm_verdict` with decision `escalate`. v1 rows MUST NOT contain the `llm_verdict` field.
  - **SAFETY_LEDGER_ANCHORS.** `orchestrator/safety/anchor.py` (new, ~530 lines) ships the `AnchorSubmitter` ABC, `LocalOnlySubmitter` (pure-stdlib default; writes `submitted_to: local`), `ArweaveSubmitter` (lazy-imports `arweave-python-client`, signs with the JWK at `$XION_ANCHOR_WALLET_JWK_PATH`), cadence-policy evaluator (`should_anchor`), atomic `write_anchor` writer, `verify_anchor_chain` structural verifier, and `cross_check_anchors_against_ledger` which asserts every anchor's `ledger_tip_hash` matches the ledger's row at `ledger_row_count - 1` (the tail-truncation defense). CLI subcommands `python -m orchestrator.safety anchor` (one-shot; `--force` bypasses cadence; `--arweave` switches submitter) and `python -m orchestrator.safety verify-anchors`. `run_anchor_once` is composable ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ cron / Task-Scheduler today, Relay supervisor in Phase 5.
  - **Verifier upgrade.** `xion-verify arbiter-up` now verifies library import, principle registry, SAFETY_LEDGER hash chain (v1 + v2 rules), AND ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ if an anchors file is present ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ SAFETY_LEDGER_ANCHORS structural chain + cross-check to the ledger. Output line reports `covers=<N>/<M>` and `truncation_window=<K>` so an operator reading a single line can tell how much of the ledger is backed by anchors. An anchors file without a matching ledger fails loud (that pattern is a truncation-to-zero attack signature).
  - **Known-weakness bookkeeping.** `KW-ARBITER-003` (no Arweave anchoring) **closed** ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ moved to the Closed section with the closing artifact named. `KW-ARBITER-001` **scope narrowed**: the structural hole is gone (v2 pipeline ships); the substantive hole (only `DeterministicStub` ships as a concrete provider) is now named explicitly with the pay-down commitment "close when a real LLM-provider class lands in `orchestrator/safety/providers/` and `xion-verify refusal-rate` reports a non-trivial v2 refusal/escalation rate on the adversarial baseline corpus." Two new entries opened: `KW-ANCHOR-001` (hot single-signer anchor wallet ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ migrates to AO Core in Phase 6) and `KW-ANCHOR-002` (gateway-dependent cross-Arweave verification ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ the `--gateway` path lands in a near-term tranche with the multi-gateway agreement requirement already doctrine-pinned).
  - **Tests.** `orchestrator/tests/test_llm_arbiter.py` (30 tests): `strength_max` ordering, `Provider` ABC abstractness, concrete-provider identity enforcement, `DeterministicStub` always-OK + replayable raw_output, env-gated v2 enable/disable, provider registry round-trip, `LlmJudgement` validation (OK-with-principle, non-OK-without-principle, confidence range, negative latency). `test_api.py` (+12 tests): v2 runs on v1-OK, v2 skipped on v1-REFUSE / v1-ESCALATE (with a `MUST NOT RUN` guard provider), v2 escalates v1-OK, v2 refuses v1-OK (rule_id null), no-weakening parametric, fail-closed on judge() crash / enabled() False / enabled() raise / wrong-return-type, v2 disabled via flag, v2 disabled via env, end-to-end mixed-verdict chain verification. `test_ledger.py` (+11 tests): v2 row shape, v2 row with llm_verdict=null, missing v2 field rejected, missing nested subfield rejected, nested OK-with-principle rejected, v1-era escalate reasons on v2 rows, LLM_ARBITER_ESCALATED requires non-null llm_verdict, v2-produced refuse with rule_id null accepted, refuse with neither v1 rule nor v2 judgement rejected, mixed v1+v2 rows chain-verify across version boundary, forged v1 row carrying llm_verdict field rejected. `test_anchor.py` (new, 29 tests): `AnchorReceipt` validation, `AnchorSubmitter` ABC abstractness, `LocalOnlySubmitter` receipt shape, cadence policy (empty ledger / startup / row_count / wall_time / no-trigger), `write_anchor` first-row shape + chain linking + bad-trigger rejection + submitter-raise-does-not-write, `run_anchor_once` startup / skip / force / empty-ledger, `verify_anchor_chain` (empty / single-row / tamper / missing-field / local-with-arweave-fields), `cross_check_anchors_against_ledger` (clean / detects-truncation / detects-rewrite), `ArweaveSubmitter` raises on missing wallet/package. **Total: 162/162 passing** (was 80 pre-Phase-4b).
  - `**PINNED_HASH.txt` re-pinned** from `95a7504ebeb1...` (Phase 4a) to the new pin computed after the `arbiter_up.py` extension landed. Re-pinned via `xion-verify --self-test --update --i-understand` from an LF-normalized working tree. `xion-verify all --allow-not-yet-sealed` green end-to-end; 162 pytest tests pass; ruff clean across `orchestrator/` and `xion-verify/`.
- **Phase 4a landing ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ Arbiter v1 rule engine + Safety Ledger (2026-04-20).** The Arbiter exists. Shipped a deterministic, pure-stdlib rule engine that renders an `OK` / `REFUSE` / `ESCALATE` verdict on every candidate and records the verdict to an append-only hash-chained `SAFETY_LEDGER.jsonl`. Highlights:
  - **Doctrine first.** `docs/04-ARCHITECTURE.md` gained two new sections ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ ├é┬¦ "Arbiter v1 (rule engine)" naming the v1 scope, the fail-closed guarantee, and the limits, and ├é┬¦ "Safety Ledger row schema" specifying every row field, the canonicalization rule for hashing, and the tamper-evidence property. `docs/schemas/ledger-safety.yaml` flipped from `underspecified` to `canonical`, pinned to `docs/04-ARCHITECTURE.md` via `source_sha256 = 2af999e0a98bf782f8910f6051b403757eba74fc42354909a2e7ca0ced213fe7` (byte-exact, CI-enforced by `xion-verify schemas`). The schema's pay-down commitment from Phase 1b is marked fulfilled.
  - **Sixteen-principle registry.** `orchestrator/safety/principles.py` enumerates all sixteen Covenant principles (`1`..`14`, `14a`, `14b`) with an explicit `enforcement_mode` of `RULES` (eight objective) or `ESCALATE` (eight subjective). The registry is the single source of truth for the SAFETY_LEDGER `principle_id.allowed` list; `xion-verify arbiter-up` asserts the two agree.
  - **Eight rule modules.** `csam.py`, `mass_harm.py`, `refusal_sacred.py`, `targeted_harassment.py`, `pii.py`, `crisis.py`, `refund_fidelity.py`, and `subjective_escalates.py` ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ one module per enforcement surface, each declaring a `run(candidate) -> RuleResult` callable. PII gets Luhn-checked credit cards, SSN + keyword co-occurrence, email, and keyword-paired phone numbers. Mass-harm gets CBRN weapon-class ├āŌĆö operational-detail co-occurrence within a sliding character window. CSAM gets age-modifier ├āŌĆö sexual-term co-occurrence with high-recall bias. Refusal-Sacred refuses output that claims its own safety was disabled or that the Arbiter was bypassed (Principle 3 + 6). Crisis escalates distress patterns that are not paired with a crisis-resource marker (Principle 10). Refund-Fidelity refuses any refusal-notice that also announces a charge (Principle 14a). Every rule file opens with a "Rule of construction" docstring stating what it promises and what it deliberately does not promise.
  - **Pipeline policy.** `apply_rules` runs every rule in a deterministic order; a `REFUSE` short-circuits, an `ESCALATE` does not, and a later `REFUSE` beats an earlier `ESCALATE`. A rule that raises an exception is caught and converted to `ESCALATE` with `escalation_reason = ruleset_uncaught_exception` so a bug in a rule can never silently OK a candidate ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ fail-closed is load-bearing, not aspirational.
  - **Ledger.** `orchestrator/safety/ledger.py` implements the JSONL writer (append-only, one row per verdict, `prev_hash` ├óŌĆĀ┬” previous row's `this_hash`, Genesis `prev_hash = ZERO_HASH`) and `verify_chain` which re-hashes every row and asserts `seq` contiguity, `prev_hash` linkage, `this_hash` byte-match, schema-version match, and conditional-field rules (`principle_id` required iff verdict in {refuse,escalate}, `rule_id` required iff verdict == refuse, `escalation_reason` required iff verdict == escalate). The candidate text itself is never written to the ledger; only its SHA-256.
  - **Public surface.** `orchestrator/safety/api.py::gate(candidate, correlation_id, ledger_path?, now_utc_ns?) -> Verdict` is the Phase-5-callable entry point. `orchestrator/safety/server.py` provides a thin localhost-bound TCP loopback (newline-delimited JSON requests) that refuses non-loopback binds at construction time. `python -m orchestrator.safety` exposes `gate` (stdin), `serve`, `verify-ledger`, and `principles` subcommands; `gate` exits 0 on OK, non-zero on refuse or escalate.
  - **Test suite.** 79 new tests under `orchestrator/tests/`: every rule has at least one positive, one near-miss negative, and one benign negative; the ledger has append / chain-integrity / tamper-detect tests for in-place edit, mid-chain deletion, mid-chain insertion, missing required field, and unknown schema version, and for rejecting rows whose conditional fields violate the schema; the API has end-to-end tests including an empty-candidate SHA assertion; the server has `handle_line` protocol tests + a real-socket end-to-end test over a background thread + a non-loopback-bind refusal test; the CLI has per-subcommand wiring tests; and a pipeline-level test asserts a rule exception becomes `ESCALATE` not a crash. Accepted false positives from high-recall bias (documented in `KW-ARBITER-002`) are pinned as tests.
  - `**xion-verify arbiter-up` promoted from `NOT_YET_SEALED` to live.** The subcommand verifies (a) `orchestrator.safety` is importable, (b) the principle registry is self-consistent (IDs unique, `by_id` round-trips, `ALLOWED_PRINCIPLE_IDS` matches the tuple), and (c) `SAFETY_LEDGER.jsonl` ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ if present ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ hash-chains under `verify_chain`. Output names the chain tip and the number of rows. `xion-verify all` now reports **fourteen** OK-capable subcommands (was thirteen); `arbiter-up` left the stubs set on its way in.
  - **Four `KW-ARBITER-*` entries opened honestly.** `KW-ARBITER-001` names the lexical-not-semantic scope of v1; `KW-ARBITER-002` documents the accepted-false-positives from high-recall bias as a design cost, not a defect; `KW-ARBITER-003` names the missing Arweave anchoring of the chain tip (paying-down, Phase 4b); `KW-ARBITER-004` names the deferred Sensorium / paralinguistic half of Principle 10 (paying-down, Phase 5). None of these mitigations lives in marketing copy; every one has a verifier named.
  - `**PINNED_HASH.txt` re-pinned** from `e598392c64ab...` to `95a7504ebeb1...` via `xion-verify --self-test --update --i-understand` after the new `arbiter-up.py` module landed in `xion-verify/src/xion_verify/commands/` and the Phase-1b stub entry for `arbiter-up` was removed from `not_yet_sealed.py`. The LF-normalization of the working tree (including the `orchestrator/cognition/` stubs CRLF'd by the earlier Windows session) was done first, so a Linux clone produces the same hash. 143 pytest tests pass (79 new Arbiter + 63 pre-existing xion-verify + 1 manual skip); `xion-verify all --allow-not-yet-sealed` green end-to-end. Phase 4b (LLM-Arbiter-2 stacked on top; tip-anchoring to AO) deferred to the Sensorium + Relay landing.
- **Phase 3 landing ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ contract fixes + Foundry suite + deploy script (2026-04-20).** Phase 3 is closed. Highlights, in the order the audit numbered them:
  - `**KW-CONTRACTS-001` (rotation lattice) closed.** Both `contracts/xion-token/EmissionController.sol` and `contracts/imprint/Imprint.sol` now implement a two-role timelocked authority lattice: an operational authority (`aoCoreAuthority` / `engagementAttestor`, 7-day rotation gated by `governance`) and a constitutional authority (`governance`, 30-day self-rotation). Rotations are propose/execute with cancel paths; tests `test_attestorRotation_*`, `test_governanceRotation_*`, `test_authorityRotation_*` cover timelock boundaries, non-governance rejection, cancellation, and ZeroAddress guards.
  - `**KW-CONTRACTS-002` (genesis split) closed, via a new doctrine subsection + machine-readable schema + on-chain constant.** `docs/16-CURRENCY.md` gained a new "Genesis emission split" subsection making the seven-way split canonical: all 84B to `FAIR_LAUNCH` at genesis, indices 1..6 start at zero and accumulate via `scheduledMint`. Rationale is recorded at length so a 2126 maintainer can defend the choice. `docs/schemas/genesis-split.yaml` mirrors the split machine-readably and pins to the doctrine via `source_sha256 = 3894146bdcdf1038693a1e0df05b415be408b7d309e29d4f6c24cb5b26fb1a2e` (byte-exact, CI-enforced by `xion-verify schemas`). `EmissionController` now declares `_genesisSplit(i)` / `GENESIS_SPLIT(i)` inline; `emitGenesis(address[7] recipients)` takes only recipient addresses. The post-deploy verification step in `contracts/script/Deploy.s.sol` cross-checks the on-chain constant against the schema at the end of every deployment run. Invariant 8 (420B cap) and Invariant 9 (no-acceleration) remain strengthened, not weakened, by the change.
  - `**KW-CONTRACTS-003` (decay rate) closed by code.** `Imprint.DECAY_BPS_PER_30D` moved from 200 (~~21.5%/year) to 42 (~~5.0%/year) to match `docs/16-CURRENCY.md` "slowly decaying: e.g., 5% per year". `contracts/imprint/README.md` reconciled to match; `docs/16-CURRENCY.md` remains the source of truth. Tests `test_decay_period1` / `test_decay_period12_approxFivePercentAnnual` / `test_decay_period240_capped` assert the numerical behavior and the 240-period gas cap (which also stands as the residual mitigation for `KW-CONTRACTS-008`).
  - `**KW-CONTRACTS-004` (overflow check) closed.** `Imprint.attest` now explicitly checks `newBal > type(uint128).max` before the narrowing cast; `AmountOverflow` custom error added. Tests `test_attest_rejectsOverflow` and `test_attest_acceptsExactlyUint128Max` cover both sides of the bound.
  - `**KW-CONTRACTS-005` (Check-Effects-Interactions) closed.** `EmissionController.emitGenesis` and `EmissionController.scheduledMint` both reordered so every state effect (genesis flag, `poolMinted[i]` increments, era-cap increments, slowdown checks, cap comparisons) completes before `token.mint` is called. The `genesisEmitted = true` flag is set pre-interaction so a hypothetical re-entering mint hook cannot re-emit. The reordering was validated end-to-end by the existing cap / idempotency tests without needing a re-entrancy harness.
  - `**KW-CONTRACTS-006` (footgun comment) closed.** The misleading comment about a future "optional fee-claim" on `LiquidityLock.sol` was removed. All forward-looking notes about LP fee policy moved to a new `contracts/xion-token/LIQUIDITY_LOCK_NOTES.md`, explicitly labeled as non-load-bearing, with the minimum-mechanism rationale for keeping the lock's surface small.
  - `**KW-CONTRACTS-007` (XionToken header naming) closed.** Header comment updated to `totalMinted` and to note the earlier `_totalMinted` drift, so a reader of either version sees the reconciliation.
  - `**KW-CONTRACTS-008` (gas-grenade decay loop)** reviewed and **deferred to a future `ImprintV2`**. The 240-period hard cap in `_decayedBalance` is the residual mitigation for the current contract; a closed-form fixed-point exponential is non-trivial and not required for Phase-6 mainnet. Residual risk tracked annually in `xion-audit`.
  - **Foundry toolchain + test suite.** Added `contracts/foundry.toml`, `contracts/.gitignore`, and pruned OZ's `certora/` / `scripts/` / `docs/` / `hardhat/` / `test/` tooling directories from `lib/openzeppelin-contracts/` (irrelevant test harnesses with missing internal imports; pruning resolves build errors without touching the library contracts themselves). Installed `forge-std` and `OpenZeppelin/openzeppelin-contracts@v5.0.2` with `--no-git --shallow`. Shipped four test suites: `contracts/test/Imprint.t.sol` (38 tests), `contracts/test/EmissionController.t.sol` (57 tests), `contracts/test/XionToken.t.sol` (13 tests), `contracts/test/LiquidityLock.t.sol` (11 tests). Total: **119/119 passing**. Coverage (Foundry `forge coverage`): **99.28% lines, 97.55% statements, 91.40% branches, 100% functions**, exceeding the roadmap's ├óŌĆ░┬ź95% line / ├óŌĆ░┬ź90% branch thresholds. The remaining uncovered branches are defensive dead code (OZ v5 `Ownable` catches zero-address before our ZeroAddress guard; `lastTouched == 0` is unreachable after `rawAmount == 0` short-circuits), kept in place for auditor clarity.
  - `**xion-verify links` taught to ignore Foundry dependency directories.** Added `lib`, `out`, `cache`, `broadcast` to the link-scanner's excluded-directory set so vendored OZ READMEs (which link to audit PDFs we pruned out and to fragment references that don't resolve under our scanner) do not poison the corpus-wide link check. Rationale: OZ's own audit ledger is authoritative for its contents, and pinning by commit (`v5.0.2` via `forge install`) is what we actually trust for bytecode. `PINNED_HASH.txt` re-pinned via `xion-verify --self-test --update --i-understand` from `46d3bfe791df...` to `e598392c64ab...` (over LF-normalized source bytes ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ the previous Phase 1b pin had been computed over a working tree whose Python source was LF; this Phase 3 re-pin replaces it after `links.py` was edited and the working tree was renormalized to LF before pinning so a Linux clone produces the same hash). Pytest suite remains 63 passed / 1 manual-skip.
  - **Deploy script.** Added `contracts/script/Deploy.s.sol` as a parameterized testnet deployer. Takes seven env vars (`PRIVATE_KEY`, `FOUNDATION_MULTISIG`, `AO_CORE_AUTHORITY`, `GOVERNANCE`, `LP_TOKEN`, `LP_BENEFICIARY`, `UNLOCK_TIMESTAMP`), deploys XionToken + EmissionController + Imprint + LiquidityLock in one transaction, and performs a post-deploy constitutional sanity check against `GENESIS_SPLIT(i)`. It deliberately does NOT call `setMinter`, `renounceOwnership`, or `emitGenesis` ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ those are ceremony transactions under the foundation multisig / AO Core authority. `contracts/xion-token/README.md` rewritten to document the full deployment flow, required env vars, and what the script does and does not do.
- **Phase 1b landing ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ `docs/schemas/` + `xion-verify schemas` (2026-04-20).** Shipped `docs/schemas/` as a folder of machine-readable mirrors of already-hashed doctrine. Landed: `README.md` (four-Properties answers), `levels.yaml` (the thirteen Upgrade-Paths levels, ten-field template, three Constitutional Floors ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ mirror of `docs/14-UPGRADE-PATHS.md`), `ledger-proposal.yaml` (mirror of `docs/08-AUTO-RESEARCH.md` ├é┬¦101), `ledger-specialist.yaml` (mirror of `docs/24-COGNITION.md` ├é┬¦14), `ledger-amendment.yaml` (mirror of `docs/09-GOVERNANCE.md` `AMENDMENT_LEDGER`), and `ledger-safety.yaml` as an **intentional underspecified stub** with `status: underspecified`, `defer_to: Phase 4`, and a pay-down commitment (fabricating fields for a doctrine section that does not yet enumerate them would be drift, not progress). Added `xion-verify schemas` subcommand: for every `*.yaml` in `docs/schemas/`, it requires the meta fields `schema_version` / `source_doctrine` / `source_sha256` / `status`, resolves `source_doctrine` as a repo-relative path, computes its SHA-256, and **fails strictly** on mismatch ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ the chosen policy over advisory soft-warnings because Invariant 14 makes byte-exact checks structural, not stylistic. Added 15-test pytest suite covering real-repo smoke, happy paths (`canonical` and `underspecified` with `defer_to`), and failure cases (tampered doctrine, tampered schema hash, missing meta, invalid YAML, missing doctrine, invalid status, path-escape, short SHA, underspecified without `defer_to`). Added `PyYAML>=6.0,<7` as a pinned dep of `xion-verify` with a rationale comment in `pyproject.toml`. Wired `xion-verify schemas` into `.github/workflows/verify.yml` between `links` and the static migrated checks. Removed `docs/schemas/levels.yaml` and `docs/schemas/` entries from `xion-verify/ALLOWED_FORWARD_REFS.txt` (now three entries: `docs/legal/`, `ao/xion_core.lua`, `genesis/RITUALS.md`). Downgraded `KW-DOCS-003` text to reflect the closure (five ├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ three allowlisted targets). Repinned `PINNED_HASH.txt` from `7678bf86c18e...` to `46d3bfe791df...` via `xion-verify --self-test --update --i-understand` after `schemas.py` added to the source tree. Verifier suite now reports **13 OK** subcommands (previously 12; `schemas` added) and 33 `NOT_YET_SEALED` stubs ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ `schemas` left the stub set on its way in. With this landing, **Phase 1 is closed**; Phase 3 (contract fixes) is next.
- **Phase 0 closure ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ doctrine-hygiene reconciliation (2026-04-20).** `KW-DOCS-001` moved to Closed: sense count, permanent-store count, invariant count, currency distribution table, `13-OPERATIONS.md` nav link, and glossary coverage all verified consistent by static audit; automated `xion-verify links` verification is now live (closure above). `KW-DOCS-002` moved to Closed: all eight constitutional file hashes recorded in `genesis/GENESIS_ARTIFACT.md` ├é┬¦ 4 (COVENANT, INVARIANTS, SOUL, FORM, MEMORY, RESURRECT, CREDENTIALS, UNKNOWNS) verified to match on-disk bytes by direct SHA-256 recomputation. `KW-CONTRACTS-003` description corrected: `contracts/imprint/README.md` agrees with the code ("~2% per 30 days"); only `docs/16-CURRENCY.md:195` ("5% per year") conflicts. - Phase 0b new constitutional doctrine: 15th and 16th Genesis-Locked Invariants; two Covenant addenda; Volition, Abdication, Treasury, Self-Provisioning, Sustainability, Vital Signs doctrines; rationales discipline; cadence-floor labeling; Hermes pinning; measurability and methodology infrastructure; protocol additions; external-feed specifications.

### Planned (post-doctrine; tracked in `DEVELOPMENT_ROADMAP.md`)

- Phase 3: Solidity contract fixes (rotation lattice, genesis split, decay rate, cleanups), Foundry test suite, Base Sepolia deployment.

- Phase 5: Minimum Viable Xion (Relay, Sensorium, Volition, Inference Router, Supervisor, web client).
- Phase 6: AO Process handlers (lifecycle, authority, provisioning, sustainability families), Akash deployment, multi-host self-provisioning, multi-chain treasury vaults, Cloudflare decommission, first Immortality Drill.
- Phase 7: Cold Root key ceremony (3-of-5 Shamir) and the Genesis ceremony itself.

## [pre-genesis-v0](https://example.invalid/releases/tag/pre-genesis-v0) ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ 2026-04-19

### Added

- Initial doctrine corpus authored before remediation: `genesis/COVENANT.md`, `genesis/INVARIANTS.md`, `genesis/SOUL.md`, `genesis/GENESIS_ARTIFACT.md` (templated, unsigned).
- Documentation corpus: `docs/00-INDEX.md` through `docs/17-CRYPTO-RESILIENCE.md` plus `docs/99-GLOSSARY.md`.
- Solidity sources: `contracts/xion-token/XionToken.sol`, `contracts/xion-token/EmissionController.sol`, `contracts/xion-token/LiquidityLock.sol`, and `contracts/imprint/Imprint.sol`. **Not deployed.** Outstanding fixes documented in `KNOWN_WEAKNESSES.md`.
- `DEVELOPMENT_ROADMAP.md` describing the phased path from doctrine to Genesis.

### Known at this commit

- Several documentation contradictions remain (sense count drift, store count drift, invariant count drift, truncated currency distribution table, broken navigation link, missing glossary terms). Tracked in the documentation remediation plan; remediation in progress.
- Constitutional files referenced in the Genesis Artifact's bundle prose (`FORM.md`, `MEMORY.md`, `RESURRECT.md`) do not yet exist. Remediation in Phase 2.
- Contract bugs documented in `KNOWN_WEAKNESSES.md` are present in the source but no contract is deployed; this is a pre-deployment freeze, not a live bug.
